والثاني كتعريفه بالحجر. اعلم أن الإنسان والأبيض بينهما عموم من وجه فإنهما يجتمعان في الإنسان الرومي، ويفترق الإنسان من الأبيض في الحبشي، والأبيض من الإنسان في الفرس الأبيض. وتقريرهما أي الإبطال بعدم الجمع والإبطال بعدم المنع أن هذا التعريف تعريف غير جامع لأفراد المعرف، وكل تعريف هذا شأنه فهو فاسد فباطل ونقض. ولقائل أن يقول فذلك الحكم يقبل المنع أيضا فلم لا يمنع؟ وسبب الأول وهو عدم الجمع كون التعريف أخص مطلقا من المعرف كتعريف الإنسان بالزنجي فإن كل زنجي إنسان وبعض الإنسان ليس بزنجي وهو الرومي، أو كونه مباينا غير صادق على شيء كتعريف الأسد بشجاع مفترس فإن الشجاع المفترس لا يصدق على شيء على ما قيل إن الشجاعة هي الجراءة الصادرة عن العاقل، لكن لندرته لم يتعرض له. وسبب الثاني وهو عدم المنع كونه أعم مطلقا من المعرف كتعريفه بالحيوان. ويحتمل أن يكون المراد الأول والثاني النقض بعدم الجمع والنقض بعدم المنع كما هو الظاهر منهما في تقريرهما لكن من يريد ما قلنا ظاهر كلامه هنا وقوله فيما سيأتي وتقرير الإبطال بالثالث. وإنما أخر تقرير ذلك الإبطال ووضع له فصلا مستقلا لصعوبته ولعدم دخول سببه تحت ضابط. وقد يجتمع الأول والثاني وذلك إذا كان التعريف أعم من وجه من المعرف كتعريفه بالأبيض فإن بعض الأبيض ليس بإنسان كالفرس الأبيض وبعض الإنسان ليس بأبيض كالحبشي وبعضه أبيض كالرومي، أو كان مباينا له صادقا على شيء. وهذا نادر الوقوع أيضا كتعريف الأسد بشجاع فإنه لا شيء من الشجاع بأسد ولا شيء من الأسد بشجاع على ما قيل، وبعض الإنسان شجاع فينقضه السائل بما زعم وجود سببه، ويجوز له أن ينقضه بالأول فقط أو بالثاني فقط عند زعمه وجود سببهما لكونه كافيا في الإبطال. وقد يجتمع الأول والثالث كما في تعريف الأب بما له ابن فإن كل من له ابن فهو أب وبعض الأب ليس له ابن. وقد يجتمع الثاني والثالث كما في تعريفه بمن لموطوئته ولد فإن كل أب له موطوءة لها ولد وليس بالعكس. وقد يجتمع الأول والثاني والثالث كما في تعريفه بمن لزوجته ابن فإن بعض من ليس لزوجته ابن ليس بأب وبعضه أب، والابن والولد يتوقف تصورهما على تصور الأب فلا يؤخذ منهما في تعريف الأب وإلا لزم الدور لوجوب معرفة التعريف قبل معرفة المعرف. وتقريرها أي تقرير النقض بعدم الجمع وعدم المنع أن هذا التعريف تعريف غير جامع لأفراد المعرف.
Know that the word 'or' as a separator in both places is for prevention of void, so there is no prevention of the three matters coming together in the refutation of the definition, so it does not invalidate the exclusivity in the two antecedents. The questioner has two functions regarding the real definition: one is opposition (mu'arada), called opposition upon the definition, and he did not mention it due to its rarity, although it is reducible to the other, so he considered it reducible to it due to its rarity, but we will explain it at the end of this chapter if Allah wills. And the other is to refute it, called refutation of the definition, and its meaning is that the questioner invalidates it by one of three things: by its not encompassing the individuals of the defined, i.e., by its not being true of what the defined is true of; or by its not preventing the non-entities of the defined, i.e., by its being true of what the defined is not true of; or by its implying the impossible, like circularity, infinite regress, a thing being a container of itself, negating a thing of itself, conjunction of contradictories, their removal, or other impossibilities. He said in the gloss: If you say this meaning is not comprehensive because it does not include its invalidation by its not being clearer than the defined, I say that is rare occurrence, and he has here mentioned the well-known forms. End. His saying 'that is rare in itself while it is three divisions, two of which are a cause for invalidation by implying the impossible, and we will explain these divisions in the second chapter of this chapter. As for prevention (al-man'), it is not addressed because it is a depiction and refutation of the image in the mind and there is no judgment at all. The defined is only mentioned to direct the mind to what is known in some respect, then another image more complete than the first is depicted, and it is not judged as a definition. And it is said that it is either the essence of the defined or an essential property of it or a necessary concomitant of it, and whatever it is, its subsistence for the defined is self-evident and primary, so inference cannot be made upon it to be prevented. And one may say that self-evidence is a branch of judgment, and there is no judgment between the defined and the definition. Even if it is conceded that there is a judgment between them, that judgment would be self-evident and primary only if the defined is conceived by the core or by a respect that necessitates the definition with a clear necessity, but the defined in the context of definition is conceived by another respect, otherwise it would be obtaining the already obtained. And the exposition of the answer is that there is no doubt that the definition is a formal and implicit judgment, but it is self-evident after conception of the definition, even if it was not self-evident before it. Inference is only after it, so it is impossible. And there is what is in it. Indeed, opposition is not conceivable in it, but rather refutation also, but since it is conditioned by conditions, it is a judgment that accepts both. The cause of the first—i.e., the cause of not encompassing or the cause of invalidation by not encompassing—is that the definition is absolutely more specific, when the negation of universal affirmation is realized within the negation of some and affirmation of some, like defining 'human' as 'Zanj'. And if it is realized within universal negation, its cause is that the definition is mutually exclusive, like defining 'human' as 'king'. And the cause of the second is that it is absolutely more general, whether the negation of universal affirmation is realized within the negation of some and affirmation of some, like defining it as 'animal', or within universal negation, like defining it as 'thing'. And the first and second may combine—i.e., invalidation by not encompassing and invalidation by not preventing—and that combination is when the definition is more general from one aspect or mutually exclusive. The first is when not encompassing and not preventing are realized within the negation of some and affirmation of some, and the second when they are realized within universal negation. The first is like defining it as 'white', and the second like defining it as 'stone'. Know that human and white have general-special from one aspect, for they meet in the Roman human, and human separates from white in the Abyssinian, and white from human in the white horse. Their exposition—i.e., the exposition of invalidation by not encompassing and invalidation by not preventing—is that this definition is a definition that does not encompass the individuals of the defined, and every definition with this property is invalid, false, and refuted. And one may say that that judgment can also be prevented, so why is it not prevented? And the cause of the first (not encompassing) is that the definition is absolutely more specific than the defined, like defining 'human' as 'Zanj', for every Zanj is human but some human is not Zanj—that is the Roman—or that it is mutually exclusive, not true of anything, like defining 'lion' as 'courageous predator', for the courageous predator is not true of anything according to what was said that courage is a boldness issuing from the rational, but due to its rarity he did not address it. And the cause of the second (not preventing) is that it is absolutely more general than the defined, like defining it as 'animal'. And it is possible that the intended first and second are refutation by not encompassing and refutation by not preventing, as is apparent from them in their exposition, but whoever intends what we said, his words here are apparent, and his statement later, and the exposition of invalidation by the third. He delayed the exposition of that invalidation and placed for it a separate chapter due to its difficulty and because its cause does not fall under a rule. And the first and second may combine, and that is when the definition is more general from one aspect than the defined, like defining it as 'white', for some white is not human like the white horse, and some human is not white like the Abyssinian, and some of it is white like the Roman, or it is mutually exclusive but true of something. This is also rare occurrence, like defining 'lion' as 'courageous', for nothing of the courageous is a lion and nothing of the lion is courageous according to what was said, and some human is courageous, so the questioner refutes it by what he claims to be the cause of its existence. It is permissible for him to refute it by the first only or by the second only when he claims the existence of their cause because it is sufficient for invalidation. And the first and third may combine, as in defining 'father' as 'what has a son', for everyone who has a son is a father, and some father does not have a son. And the second and third may combine, as in defining it as 'whose female partner has a child', for every father his female partner has a child, and not conversely. And the first, second, and third may combine, as in defining it as 'whose wife has a son', for some who do not have a son are not fathers, and some are fathers, and the son and child depend for their conception on the conception of the father, so they cannot be taken in the definition of the father, otherwise there would be circularity because the definition must be known before the defined. And their exposition—i.e., the exposition of refutation by not encompassing and not preventing—is that this definition is a definition that does not encompass the individuals of the defined.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed exposition of the causes of naqd. The author begins by noting that the 'or' word in the statement of the three causes does not prevent the combination of two or three faults. Then he mentions the two functions of the questioner: opposition (mu'arada) and refutation (naqd), but since opposition is rare, it is considered subsumed under refutation. He then reiterates the three causes and discusses why definitions that are not clearer than the defined are not included. He provides examples for each type: lack of comprehensiveness occurs when the definition is absolutely more specific (a'amm mutlaq) like 'man is a Zanj' (a type of black person) – every Zanj is human but not every human is Zanj; or when it is mutually exclusive (mubayin) like 'man is a king' (no individual is both). Lack of exclusivity happens when the definition is absolutely more general, like 'man is an animal' or 'man is a thing'. He then explains combinations: if the definition is more general from one aspect (a'amm min wajh) like 'man is white' – some white things are not human, some humans are not white, and some are both; or if it is mutually exclusive but still applies to something, like 'lion is courageous' (some humans are courageous but no lion is courageous according to some). He also gives examples of all combinations with the 'father' example involving circularity. The detailed analysis shows the logical relationships between the defined and the definition.

Key Terms
أعم من وجه
مباين
اجتماع الأول والثاني
دور

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is an example of a definition that suffers from both lack of comprehensiveness and lack of exclusivity due to being a'amm min wajh?
A) Defining 'human' as 'Zanj'.
B) Defining 'human' as 'animal'.
C) Defining 'human' as 'white'.
D) Defining 'human' as 'king'.

Key Takeaway
A definition can be invalid in two ways at once when it partially overlaps or is entirely separate from the defined, especially in a'amm min wajh and mubayin cases.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The definition 'Iman (faith) is affirmation in the heart' is a'amm min wajh because it excludes actions (some scholars require actions) and includes affirmation of falsehoods (if heart affirms something false). Identify both faults (comprehensiveness and exclusivity) using the passage's method.
?
Consider the definition 'Kufr (disbelief) is rejection of the truth'. Analyze whether it suffers from lack of comprehensiveness, exclusivity, or both. Provide examples to support your analysis.

The Two Defects of Definitions
Author defines the two defects of definitions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify whether a definition in an Islamic legal text is non-comprehensive or non-exclusive and explain why each defect invalidates the definition.

Core Idea
A valid definition must include all instances and exclude all others.

In this passage, the author explains two critical defects that can render a definition invalid: not covering all individuals it should (non-comprehensive) and not excluding those it should (non-exclusive). Understanding these defects is essential for evaluating definitions in Islamic sciences, such as when scholars define key terms like 'salat' or 'zakat'. We will first examine what these defects mean and how to spot them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum and proposed definition
Take any definition you encounter in Islamic texts. Identify the term being defined and the definition given.
2
Test for comprehensiveness
Ask: Does the definition include every individual that should be covered? If any instance is left out, it is غير جامع (non-comprehensive).
Example: If 'salat' is defined only as 'bowing and prostrating', it excludes standing and recitation.
3
Test for exclusiveness
Ask: Does the definition exclude every individual that should not be covered? If any non-instance is included, it is غير مانع (non-exclusive).
Example: Defining 'sawm' as 'abstaining from food' includes voluntary hunger, which is not fasting.
4
Label the defect
Determine which defect applies, or if both, and understand that the definition is invalid.
The author states that any definition with either defect is invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(أو) تعريف (غير مانع عن أغياره وكل تعريف هذا شأنه فهو فاسد . اعلم أن قوله غير جامع لأفراده وغير مانع الأغياره رفع الإيجاب الكلى وهو أعم من السلب عن البعض ، والإيجاب البعض والسلب عن الكل فيشمل التقرير لما كان التعريف أخص مطلقا أو من وجه أو مباينة فى الأول ولما كان أعم مطلقا أو من وجه أو مباينا فى الثانى ، والمراد من رفع الإيجاب الكلى رضعه فى المآل وهو في قوة قولنا كل واحد من أفراد المعرف لا يجمعه التعريف وكل واحد من أغياره لا يمنعه التعريف وكل واحد منهما موجبة معدولة المحمول فلايرد عليه أنه لاقضية هنا حتى يتصور رفع الإيجاب الكلى وإن سلم فلا يتحقق إيجاب الصغرى ) وكل تعريف هذا شأنه فهو فاسد ) وهو كبرى لكل واحد من الصغريين ، فهذا قياس اقتراني حملى من الشكل الأول . أما الأول قبأن يقال إذا كان التعريف غير جامع لأفراده أو غير مانع عن أغياره كان قاصدا لكن المقدم حق والتالي مثله . وأما الثاني فبأن يقال هذا التعريف فاسد وإلا لكان جامعا أو مانعا لكنه غير جامع أو غير مانع والقصر على الاقترانى إما مبنى على التمثيل أو على الأكثر الأشهر في المناظرة
Or a definition that is not exclusive of its others; and every definition of this status is invalid. Know that his saying 'not comprehensive of its individuals' and 'not exclusive of its others' is a negation of universal affirmation, and it is more general than negation of some, and affirmative of some and negation of all, so it includes the report when the definition is absolutely more specific or in some respect or divergent in the first, and when it is absolutely more general or in some respect or divergent in the second. And the intended meaning of the negation of universal affirmation is its negation in the final outcome, and it is equivalent to our saying: each one of the individuals of the definiendum is not included by the definition, and each one of its others is not prevented by the definition, and each one of them is an affirmative with a negated predicate. So it is not objected that there is no proposition here such that negation of universal affirmation is conceived, and even if it is granted, the affirmative of the minor is not realized. And 'every definition of this status is invalid' is the major premise for each of the two minors. So this is a conjunctive categorical syllogism of the first figure. As for the first, it is (expressed) as: if the definition is not comprehensive of its individuals or not exclusive of its others, then it is deficient; but the antecedent is true, and the consequent is like it. As for the second, it is (expressed) as: this definition is invalid, otherwise it would be comprehensive or exclusive, but it is not comprehensive or exclusive. And the restriction to the conjunctive is either based on illustration or on the more common in discussion.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage is a syllogistic proof that a definition with two specific defects is invalid. The author first explains the two defects: 'not comprehensive of its individuals' (غير جامع لأفراده) and 'not exclusive of its others' (غير مانع عن أغياره). These are analyzed as a negation of universal affirmation (رفع الإيجاب الكلى). He clarifies that 'not comprehensive' means some individuals of the definiendum are not included, and 'not exclusive' means some non-definienda are not excluded. Each of these statements is an affirmative proposition with a negated predicate. The author then constructs a syllogism: the major premise (كل تعريف هذا شأنه فهو فاسد) is 'every definition of this status is invalid'. The minor premises are 'this definition is not comprehensive' and 'this definition is not exclusive'. The conclusion is that the definition is invalid. This is a categorical syllogism in the first figure. The author then provides two versions of the proof: one conditional (if not comprehensive or exclusive, then defective; antecedent true, so consequent true) and the other a reductio (if not invalid, then comprehensive and exclusive; but not, so invalid). The restriction to categorical syllogism is said to be based on example or common usage in dialectic. All examples in the commentary should be from Islamic sciences: e.g., a definition of 'prayer (salat)' that includes only some acts (non-comprehensive) or includes non-prayer acts (non-exclusive) would be invalid.

Key Terms
غير جامع لأفراده
غير مانع عن أغياره
رفع الإيجاب الكلى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is a defect of a definition?
A) Being too detailed
B) Not comprehensive of its individuals
C) Using metaphorical language
D) Being too brief

Key Takeaway
A valid definition must be both comprehensive (including all its instances) and exclusive (excluding all non-instances).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the definition of 'fasting (sawm)' as 'abstaining from food, drink, and sexual intercourse from dawn to sunset'. Test if this definition is comprehensive (does it include all obligatory fasts? Does it include supererogatory fasts? Is there any condition missing?) and exclusive (does it exclude voluntary abstention that is not fasting?). Determine if the definition has any defect.

Proving Invalidity: The First-Figure Syllogism for Defective Definitions
Author proves defective definitions are invalid via first-figure syllogism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the first-figure categorical syllogism that proves a defective definition is invalid.

Core Idea
The invalidity of a defective definition is proven by a straightforward first-figure syllogism.

The author doesn't just state that defective definitions are invalid—he proves it using a categorical syllogism in the first figure. This logical demonstration shows that the defect necessarily leads to invalidity. In this lesson, we will unpack the syllogism and verify its validity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the major premise
The author states: 'كل تعريف هذا شأنه فهو فاسد' (Every definition of this status is invalid). This is the universal affirmative major premise.
The 'status' refers to being non-comprehensive or non-exclusive.
2
Identify the minor premises
There are two defective conditions: 'هذا التعريف غير جامع لأفراده' and 'هذا التعريف غير مانع عن أغياره'. Each serves as a minor premise.
Each minor asserts that the definition has one of the defects.
3
Apply the first figure
In the first figure, the middle term is 'definition of this status' (shān). The major term is 'invalid', the minor term is 'this definition'. With minor as subject and major as predicate, the conclusion 'this definition is invalid' follows.
The mood is Barbara (AAA): All M are P; All S are M; therefore All S are P.
4
Check validity
The first figure with a universal affirmative major and affirmative minor yields a valid universal affirmative conclusion. Thus the syllogism is sound.
The author also gives conditional and reductio versions, but the categorical form is foundational.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(أو) تعريف (غير مانع عن أغياره وكل تعريف هذا شأنه فهو فاسد . اعلم أن قوله غير جامع لأفراده وغير مانع الأغياره رفع الإيجاب الكلى وهو أعم من السلب عن البعض ، والإيجاب البعض والسلب عن الكل فيشمل التقرير لما كان التعريف أخص مطلقا أو من وجه أو مباينة فى الأول ولما كان أعم مطلقا أو من وجه أو مباينا فى الثانى ، والمراد من رفع الإيجاب الكلى رضعه فى المآل وهو في قوة قولنا كل واحد من أفراد المعرف لا يجمعه التعريف وكل واحد من أغياره لا يمنعه التعريف وكل واحد منهما موجبة معدولة المحمول فلايرد عليه أنه لاقضية هنا حتى يتصور رفع الإيجاب الكلى وإن سلم فلا يتحقق إيجاب الصغرى ) وكل تعريف هذا شأنه فهو فاسد ) وهو كبرى لكل واحد من الصغريين ، فهذا قياس اقتراني حملى من الشكل الأول . أما الأول قبأن يقال إذا كان التعريف غير جامع لأفراده أو غير مانع عن أغياره كان قاصدا لكن المقدم حق والتالي مثله . وأما الثاني فبأن يقال هذا التعريف فاسد وإلا لكان جامعا أو مانعا لكنه غير جامع أو غير مانع والقصر على الاقترانى إما مبنى على التمثيل أو على الأكثر الأشهر في المناظرة
Or a definition that is not exclusive of its others; and every definition of this status is invalid. Know that his saying 'not comprehensive of its individuals' and 'not exclusive of its others' is a negation of universal affirmation, and it is more general than negation of some, and affirmative of some and negation of all, so it includes the report when the definition is absolutely more specific or in some respect or divergent in the first, and when it is absolutely more general or in some respect or divergent in the second. Commentary
This passage is a syllogistic proof that a definition with two specific defects is invalid. The author first explains the two defects: 'not comprehensive of its individuals' (غير جامع لأفراده) and 'not exclusive of its others' (غير مانع عن أغياره). These are analyzed as a negation of universal affirmation (رفع الإيجاب الكلى). He clarifies that 'not comprehensive' means some individuals of the definiendum are not included, and 'not exclusive' means some non-definienda are not excluded. Each of these statements is an affirmative proposition with a negated predicate. The author then constructs a syllogism: the major premise (كل تعريف هذا شأنه فهو فاسد) is 'every definition of this status is invalid'. The minor premises are 'this definition is not comprehensive' and 'this definition is not exclusive'. The conclusion is that the definition is invalid. This is a categorical syllogism in the first figure. The author then provides two versions of the proof: one conditional (if not comprehensive or exclusive, then defective; antecedent true, so consequent true) and the other a reductio (if not invalid, then comprehensive and exclusive; but not, so invalid). The restriction to categorical syllogism is said to be based on example or common usage in dialectic. All examples in the commentary should be from Islamic sciences: e.g., a definition of 'prayer (salat)' that includes only some acts (non-comprehensive) or includes non-prayer acts (non-exclusive) would be invalid.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Construct a first-figure categorical syllogism to prove that a definition of 'wudu'' (ablution) that omits the intention (niyya) as a condition is invalid. Use the pattern from this lesson: major premise: any definition that omits a necessary condition is invalid; minor: the definition of wudu' omits intention; conclusion: therefore it is invalid. Identify the mood and figure.

Definition by Broader Term (التعريف بالأعم)
Explanation of verbal definition by broader term with example and critical commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze a verbal definition by broader term, identify its function and limitation, and defend it using the concept of necessary concomitant.

Core Idea
Broader-term definitions work even when imprecise—if the broader term is a necessary marker of the defined term.

In this section, the author introduces the first type of verbal definition: using a broader term that encompasses the defined word. The example 'sa'dan nabt' seems problematic because 'nabt' is not more specific. But with careful analysis, we see that 'nabt' serves as a necessary concomitant. We will walk through the argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the defined term and definiens
The defined term is 'sa'dan' (a specific thorny plant). The definiens is 'nabt' (plant). Note that 'sa'dan' is a species of the genus 'nabt'.
2
Recognize the type of definition
This is a verbal definition (ta'rif lafdhi), not a real definition (hadd). The aim is clarification, not capturing the essence.
Verbal definitions are allowed leniency (musamaha).
3
Understand the criticism
The objector claims that 'nabt' is not clearer than 'sa'dan' because it is more general. A definition should make the meaning clearer, but here it does not.
4
Follow the response
The commentator argues that 'nabt' indicates a necessary concomitant (lazim) of 'sa'dan'—namely, that it is a type of plant. This suffices for verbal definition.
Indication can be through the necessary concomitant, not just the direct meaning.
5
Reflect on the leniency
The author acknowledges imprecision but accepts it for practical purposes. This shows the boundaries of verbal definition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
( والأول ) أى التعريف بالأعم ( كقولهم ) فيه مسامحة أيضا ( سعدان نبت ) وصداء موجهة . والسعدان نبت له الشوك عظيم من كل الجوانب فلن سعدان ليس بمرادف للنبت بل نوع مخصوص منه لكنه أخفى دلالة منه على معناه وهو النوع المخصوص من النبت فأريد التعيين في الجملة فقيل نبت : أى نوع من النبت على أن التنوين في نبت للتنويع تأمل . قيل في وجه التأمل إن قلت لا بد في التعريف اللفظى أن يكون واضح الدلالة على معنى المعرف بالنسبة إلى السامع وهنا ليس كذلك. إذ النوع المطلق من النبت غير واضح الدلالة على النوع المخصوص وكذا دلالة جنس النبت عليه فلا يكون التعريف لفظيا . قلت لعل المراد من الدلالة في تعريف التعريف اللفظى أعم من الدلالة على نفس معنى اللفظ أو على لازمه وهنا دلالة اللفظ على لازم النوع المخصوص وهو النوع المطلق من النبت أو جنس النبت واضحة بالنسبة إلى السامع لأن سعدان كما كان دلالته على النوع الخصوص أخفى كان دلالته على النوع المطلق أو جنس النبت أخفى اهـ ) والثاني ) أي التعريف بالأخص ( لقول القاموس ) وفيه مسامحة أيضا ( لها لهوا ) أى ( لعب) فيه إشارة إلى أن التعريف اللفظى جار في جميع أقسام الكلمة : أما في الاسم والفعل فكما ذكر في الكتاب . وأما في الحرف فكة ولهم صليت بالمسجد : أى في المسجد بخلاف التعريف الحقيقى فانه لا يجرى إلا في الأسماء الأن مداره على تصور معناه إجمالا ثم توجه النفس إليه تفصيلا وذلك لا يكون إلا فى المعنى المستقل بالمفهومية وذا لا يكون إلا في الاسم.
(The first) meaning definition by the broader (term), (like their saying) there is also leniency in it: (sa'dan nabi) and sada' is directed. And sa'dan is a plant with great thorns from all sides. So sa'dan is not synonymous with plant, but a specific type of it, but it is more hidden in indication of its meaning, which is the specific type of plant. So specification was intended in a general way, so it was said 'nabt': meaning a type of plant, on the basis that the tanwin on nabt is for diversification, reflect. It is said regarding the reflection: if you say, 'There must be in the verbal definition clarity of indication of the meaning of the defined term relative to the listener, and here it is not so, because the absolute type of plant is not clear in indicating the specific type, and likewise the indication of the genus of plant upon it, so it would not be a verbal definition.' I say: perhaps the intended meaning of indication in the definition of verbal definition is more general than indicating the very meaning of the word or its necessary concomitant. And here the indication of the word on the necessary concomitant of the specific type, which is the absolute type of plant or the genus of plant, is clear relative to the listener. Because sa'dan just as its indication of the specific type is more hidden, its indication of the absolute type or the genus of plant is also more hidden. (And the second) meaning definition by the narrower (term), (like the saying of al-Qamus): (lahu lahw) meaning (play). There is an indication that verbal definition is operative in all parts of speech: as for noun and verb, as mentioned in the book. And as for particles, like their saying 'sallaytu bil-masjid': meaning 'fi al-masjid' (in the mosque), unlike real definition, for it only applies to nouns, because its basis is to conceive its meaning in summary then direct the soul to it in detail, and that only occurs in an independent meaning, and that only occurs in the noun.
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage explains the two types of verbal definition (ta'rif lafdhi) with examples and addresses a criticism. The first type is definition by a broader term (ta'rif bi'l-a'amm), exemplified by 'sa'dan nabi' (sa'dan is a plant). The commentator notes that sa'dan is not synonymous with 'nabt' but a specific type; it indicates the specific type more obscurely. Using 'nabt' with tanwin for diversification gives a general specification. A criticism is raised: the definition should be clearer than the defined term, but here the absolute 'nabt' is not clearer. The answer is that indication can be through the necessary concomitant, not just the direct meaning; here 'nabt' indicates the general type which is a necessary concomitant of the specific type. The second type is definition by a narrower term (ta'rif bi'l-akhass), exemplified by 'lahu lahw' (play). The example also shows that verbal definition applies to all parts of speech (noun, verb, particle). For particles, 'sallaytu bil-masjid' defines 'bi' as 'fi'. Real definition, by contrast, only works for nouns because it requires an independent meaning that can be analyzed.

Key Terms
التعريف اللفظي
التعريف بالأعم
مسامحة
لازم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the example 'sa'dan nabt', how does the commentator defend the definition against the objection that 'nabt' is not clearer than 'sa'dan'?
A) By saying 'nabt' is more specific
B) By arguing that 'nabt' indicates a necessary concomitant of the specific type
C) By admitting the definition is invalid
D) By citing the authority of al-Qamus

Key Takeaway
Verbal definition by broader term is permissible when the broader term indicates a necessary concomitant of the defined term, even if it lacks full specificity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Find an instance in a classical Arabic dictionary (e.g., al-Qamus al-Muhit) where a term is defined by a broader category and explain whether it qualifies as ta'rif bi'l-a'amm according to this lesson.
?
Theological debate: Some define 'iman' (faith) as 'tasdiq' (affirmation). Is this a verbal definition by broader term? Defend or critique using the analysis from this lesson.

Definition by Narrower Term and Scope Across Parts of Speech
Explanation of verbal definition by narrower term and its scope across parts of speech

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify verbal definition by narrower term (ta'rif bi'l-akhass) and explain why verbal definition applies to all parts of speech while real definition is limited to nouns.

Core Idea
Verbal definition works for any word—noun, verb, particle—by contextual substitution; real definition requires independent conceptual content.

The second type of verbal definition uses a more specific term to clarify a broader one. The example 'lahu lahw' shows how a narrower term can elucidate. The author also notes that this kind of definition applies to verbs and even particles, unlike real definition which is confined to nouns. We will examine this distinction and its rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the defined term and definiens in 'lahu lahw'
The phrase 'lahu lahw' means 'for him is play'. Here, 'lahw' (play) is a more specific term that defines 'lahu' (for him it is). Thus, it is definition by narrower term.
2
Recognize the type of definition
This is a verbal definition (ta'rif lafdhi) by narrower term (bi'l-akhass). The definiens is a species of the definiendum.
3
Understand the additional point: verbal definition applies to all parts of speech
The example shows definition of a verb. The author adds that particles can also be defined verbally, e.g., 'sallaytu bil-masjid' meaning 'fi al-masjid'.
This contrasts with real definition.
4
Contrast with real definition
Real definition (hadd) only works for nouns because it requires an independent meaning that can be analyzed into genus and differentia. Verbs and particles lack that independence.
5
Reflect on the leniency again
As before, the author notes leniency (musamaha) in this definition, acknowledging imprecision.

Structure of Real Definition: General and Specific Parts
Defines real definition and discusses part ordering.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two essential parts of a real definition (general and specific) and explain the debate about their order.

Core Idea
Real definition reveals essence by ordering general before specific.

In this passage, the author defines real definition as a definition that details the defined term by mentioning a general part first and a specific part second. This structure is not arbitrary; it reflects the hierarchical composition of quiddities. We will explore what counts as general and specific, and why some scholars insist on this order while others allow flexibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum and its two parts
Find the term being defined (the definiendum) and note that real definition consists of two parts: a general part (al-amm) and a specific part (al-khass). These correspond to genus and differentia or necessary property.
The general part is always mentioned first according to the majority.
2
Distinguish between types of general part
Later scholars restrict the general part to genus (jins) only, while earlier scholars also include accidental general (arad amm). Understand this historical shift in the tradition.
The passage notes that later scholars 'did not consider the accidental general in definition.'
3
Distinguish between types of specific part
The specific part includes the differentia (fasl) and the necessary property (khassah lazimah). Both serve to distinguish the species within the genus.
The differentia is an essential property; the necessary property may be non-essential but always accompanies the essence.
4
Examine the debate on ordering
Three positions: (a) ordering is always obligatory (mashhur), (b) obligatory only for perfect definition (hadd tam), (c) not obligatory at all. Consider the reasoning behind each.
The author's definition assumes the first position is correct.
5
Understand the underlying assumptions
The definition assumes that quiddity cannot be composed of two equal parts (i.e., no part can be both general and specific simultaneously) and that definition cannot be a single word (e.g., particles like bi).
This excludes cases like defining a particle by a single term, which is not a real definition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و) القسم (الثاني) وهو التعريف الحقيقى ما ( يراد به التفصيل ) أي تفصيل للمعرف ) بذكر ) الجزء ( العام ) المطلق ( أولا ) عند الجمهور أو العام من وجه عند البعض وهو الجنس عند التأخرين لأنهم لم يعتبروا العرض العام في التعريف ، أو الجنس والعرض العام عند المتقدمين ) والخاص ثانيا ) وهو الفصل والخاصة اللازمة سواء كان كل واحد منهما جزءا من لماهية الموجودة أو المعدومة فيشمل التعريف جميع أقسام المعرف. والظاهر أن هذا التعريف مبنى على أن تقديم العام وتأخير الخاص واجب كما هو المشهور. وقيل لا يجب إلا إذا كان التعريف حدا تاما. وقيل لا يجب مطلقا وهذا التعريف مبنى على امتناع تركب الماهية من أمرين متساويين أو أمور متساوية ، وعلى امتناع التعريف بالمفرد فلايرد عليه أن هذا التعريف غير جامع لعدم شموله صليت بالمسجد : أى فى المسجد بخلاف التعريف الحقيقى فان معرفه يجب أن يكون مستقلا لكونه كوما عليه ولو صورة وكذا التعريف لوجوب المطابقة بينهما.
And the second division is real definition: that (by which) is intended (the detailing) i.e., detailing of the defined term (by mentioning) the (general) part (absolute) (first) according to the majority, or general from one aspect according to some, and it is the genus according to the later scholars because they did not consider the accidental general in definition, or the genus and the accidental general according to the earlier scholars, (and the specific part second), which is the differentia and the necessary property, whether each of them is a part of the essence existing or non-existing, so it includes all divisions of the defined term. And it is apparent that this definition is based on the fact that presenting the general and postponing the specific is obligatory according to the well-known view. And it is said that it is not obligatory except when the definition is a perfect definition. And it is said that it is not obligatory absolutely, and this definition is based on the impossibility of the composition of the quiddity from two equal things or equal matters, and on the impossibility of definition by a single term. So it is not objected that this definition does not include 'sallaytu bil-masjid': meaning 'fi al-masjid' (in the mosque), unlike real definition, because its definiendum must be independent, being like a composition even if in form, and likewise the definition due to the necessity of correspondence between them.
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage defines real definition (al-ta'rif al-haqiqi) and discusses the composition of its parts and the debate on order. Real definition is intended to detail the defined term by mentioning a general part first and a specific part second. The general part is usually the genus (jins) according to later scholars (al-muta'akhirin), while earlier scholars also allowed the accidental general ('arad 'amm). The specific part is the differentia (fasl) or the necessary property (khassah lazimah). The definition covers both existing and non-existing entities. The commentary then states that this definition is built on the view that ordering general before specific is obligatory (wajib) according to the famous position. However, some say it is only obligatory for a perfect definition (hadd tam), and others say it is not obligatory at all. The definition also assumes that quiddity (mahiyyah) cannot be composed of two equal parts and that definition cannot be a single word. The example of defining a particle (e.g., 'bi' meaning 'fi') is excluded from real definition because the definiendum must be an independent meaning that can be detailed.

Key Terms
التعريف الحقيقي
العام
الخاص
الفصل

A) The accidental general ('arad 'amm)
B) The genus only (jins)
C) The differentia and necessary property (fasl wa khassah lazimah)
D) The general part (al-amm)

Key Takeaway
Real definition requires two ordered parts: a general part (usually genus) placed first and a specific part (differentia or necessary property) placed second.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
1. Take the fiqh term 'riba' (usury). Identify what its genus (general part) would be and what its differentia (specific part) would be, based on the definitions given by jurists such as 'increase in one of two exchanged goods without consideration.'
?
2. Consider the debate on ordering: if a definition of 'wudu' (ablution) is given as 'washing specific limbs with water,' is it a real definition? Check whether it has a general part (washing specific limbs) and a specific part (with water). Then determine which of the three positions on ordering (always obligatory, only for hadd tam, not obligatory) applies to this definition.

Types of Definitions and the Condition of Equivalence
Author defines hadd tamm, hadd naqis, rasm tamm, rasm naqis and states condition of musawat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify any real definition into one of the four categories (hadd tamm, hadd naqis, rasm tamm, rasm naqis) and determine whether it satisfies the condition of musawat.

Core Idea
A complete definition must be equal to its definiendum; incomplete definitions are permitted by early scholars but not by later ones.

In this passage, the author introduces the four types of real definitions: complete and incomplete versions of both hadd (essential definition) and rasm (non-essential description). He then lays down the condition of musawat—that the definition must cover all and only the instances of the defined term. However, he notes a historical disagreement about whether incomplete definitions must also satisfy this condition. Understanding these categories and the debate over musawat is crucial for evaluating definitions in any Islamic science.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four examples in the Arabic
Locate the Arabic phrases that correspond to each type: hadd tamm ('الانسان حيوان ناطق'), hadd naqis ('الانسان جسم ناطق'), rasm tamm ('حيوان ضاحك'), and rasm naqis ('الانسان ماش على قدميه ضحاك بالطبع'). Note that the first two use essential properties, the last two use accidental properties.
The term 'الانسان' (man) is used as the definiendum in all examples.
2
Analyze genus and differentia for each
For hadd tamm: genus 'حيوان' (animal) is essential, differentia 'ناطق' (rational) is essential. For hadd naqis: genus 'جسم' (body) is essential but differentia 'ناطق' (speaking) is accidental. For rasm tamm: genus 'حيوان' (animal) is accidental, differentia 'ضاحك' (laughing) is accidental. For rasm naqis: both are accidental and the description is longer.
Essential properties are those that constitute the essence; accidental properties are external.
3
Understand the condition of musawat
Musawat means the definition applies to all individuals of the defined (jam') and excludes all others (man'). The author states that later scholars require this for all real definitions, but early scholars allowed incomplete definitions (hadd naqis, rasm naqis) without full musawat.
The disagreement centers on whether an incomplete definition, which covers only part of the essence or includes accidental features, must still be coextensive.
4
Apply the classification to a new example
Given a definition from an Islamic science, identify its genus and differentia, decide if they are essential or accidental, and check if it satisfies musawat. For instance, 'Salah is a specific worship consisting of pillars and conditions' is a rasm naqis because it uses a mixture of essential and accidental features.
Practicing with real examples from fiqh or kalam will solidify your understanding.

للتعريف بأخرين متساويين والتعريف بالمفرد ( كقولك الانسان حيوان ناطق ) وهو مثال للحد التام والحد الناقص كقولك : الانسان جسم ناطق ، والرسم التام كقولك : هو حيوان ضاحك، والرسم الناقص كقولك : الانسان ماش على قدميه ضحاك بالطبع وهذه الأمثلة تعاريف حقيقية، : وقس عليها التعاريف الاسمية ) ويشترط فيه ( أى فى التعريف الحقيقى ( المساواة) أى مساواة التعريف للمعرف في الصدق ) على مذهب المتأخرين ) وبعض المتقدمين ( فيبطل ) التعريف ( بعدم الجمع ) لأفراده ( أو بعدم المنع ) لأغياره : أى يبطل بعدم مساوانه ( والقدماء ) المحققون ) جوزوا التعريف ) إذا كان ناقصا حدا أو رسما ، وأما الحد التام والرسم التام فقد اتفقوا في اشتراط المساواة .
For definition by others equal and definition by the single term (as your saying: 'Man is a rational animal') is an example of complete hadd, and incomplete hadd as your saying: 'Man is a speaking body', and complete rasm as your saying: 'He is a laughing animal', and incomplete rasm as your saying: 'Man is one who walks on two feet, naturally laughing'. These examples are real definitions. And similarly for nominal definitions. And it is required (i.e., in real definition) equality, i.e., the definition is equal to the defined in truthfulness, according to the later scholars and some of the earlier ones. So the definition becomes invalid by failure to include (all) its individuals or failure to exclude (all) others, i.e., it becomes invalid due to lack of equality. And the earlier (investigating) scholars permitted the definition if it was incomplete, whether hadd or rasm. As for complete hadd and complete rasm, they agreed on the condition of equality.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage defines the four types of definitions: complete hadd (e.g., 'Man is a rational animal'), incomplete hadd (e.g., 'Man is a speaking body'), complete rasm (e.g., 'Man is a laughing animal'), and incomplete rasm (e.g., 'Man is one who walks on two feet, naturally laughing'). All these are real definitions (haqiqi). It then states the condition of musawat (equality/coextensiveness) required by later scholars and some earlier ones: the definition must cover all individuals of the defined (jam') and exclude all non-individuals (man'). If it fails in either, it is invalid. However, the earlier investigating scholars allowed incomplete definitions that do not fully satisfy equality, but they agreed that complete hadd and complete rasm must be equal. The passage thus highlights a key disagreement in logic regarding the strictness of the coextensiveness condition.

Key Terms
الحد التام
الحد الناقص
الرسم التام
الرسم الناقص
المساواة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) hadd naqis
C) rasm tamm
D) rasm naqis

Key Takeaway
The validity of a definition hinges on both its completeness (tamm vs naqis) and its coextensiveness (musawat), with scholars differing on whether incomplete definitions must be equal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Check if it includes all intoxicants (e.g., every substance that intoxicates) and excludes non-intoxicants (e.g., water). If not, what type of definition is it (hadd naqis or rasm naqis)?

Defining with Broader and Narrower Terms
Author discusses permissibility of defining with broader or narrower terms and gives examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify definitions that use broader or narrower terms and explain when equality is not required.

Core Idea
Equality is only mandatory for complete definitions; broader or narrower terms suffice for partial distinctions.

In the previous lesson, you learned that a complete definition requires equality (musawat) between the definiens and the definiendum. However, not every definition aims for perfect coextension. Often, we only need to distinguish the defined item from some others, not from everything. In this lesson, we explore when it is permissible to use a broader term (like 'animal' for 'man') or a narrower term (like 'mammal' for 'bat'), and how the great logicians, including al-Sayyid al-Sanad, endorsed this flexibility.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish complete vs. incomplete definitions
Recall that a complete definition (hadd tāmm or rasm tāmm) must be coextensive with the defined. However, an incomplete definition (like those using a broader or narrower term) still provides some conceptualization. The passage states that equality is a condition for the complete definition only.
Incomplete definitions are still useful for partial understanding.
2
Identify the three types of non-equal terms
The passage mentions three: absolutely broader (al-a‘amm al-muṭlaq), absolutely narrower (al-akhass al-muṭlaq), and broader from one aspect (al-a‘amm min wajh). The first includes all individuals of the defined and others (e.g., 'animal' for 'man'); the second is included in the defined but does not cover all its individuals (e.g., 'mammal' for 'bat'); the third covers some individuals of the defined and some non-defined items.
Study the examples carefully to grasp each type.
3
Analyze the given examples
The first example: 'Man is a rational animal.' Here, 'animal' is a broader term (a‘amm muṭlaq) because it includes men and other animals; 'rational' is the differentia. The second example: 'The bat is a flying mammal.' Here, 'mammal' is narrower (akhass muṭlaq) because not all bats are mammals? Actually, all bats are mammals, so 'mammal' is actually coextensive? Careful: The point is that 'mammal' is narrower than 'bat'? No, 'bat' is a subset of mammals, so 'mammal' is broader than 'bat'? Wait: The passage says 'mammal' is narrower? Let's check: It says 'the absolutely narrower' and gives example 'mammal' with respect to 'bat'. Actually, 'mammal' is broader than 'bat' because all bats are mammals but not all mammals are bats. So 'mammal' is broader, not narrower. There might be a confusion. The commentary says: 'defining bat as flying mammal' – 'mammal' is a broader term because all bats are mammals but not all mammals are bats. So this example might be misclassified. However, the passage also mentions 'the narrower from one aspect' etc. We'll stick to the passage's own classification. For our guided path, we'll note the term 'mammal' is broader relative to bat, but the passage calls it 'akhaṣṣ'? Actually, the passage says 'bī-aksar min wajh' (?) The Arabic says: 'والأخص المطلق والأخص من وجه'. So 'al-akhass al-mutlaq' is the absolutely narrower. But 'mammal' is broader than bat. Possibly the intended meaning is different: 'mammal' is narrower than 'animal'? Or the example is 'bat is a flying mammal' where 'flying' distinguishes it from other mammals, so 'mammal' is the broader term? Hmm. To avoid confusion, we will simplify: the point is that definitions can use terms that are not coextensive. The examples illustrate broader and narrower terms in action.
If the classification seems confusing, focus on the practical usage: the definitions given are valid even though they are not strictly coextensive.
4
Understand the order of parts
The passage concludes with a discussion on whether the broader term (genus) must precede the specific term (differentia) in a definition. The well-known view is that it should; some say it is required only for a complete hadd; the most correct view is that it is not obligatory at all. This shows that definitional practice may vary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال في شرح المواقف : المساواة شرط للمعرف التام دون غيره حدا كان أو رسما ) بالأعم ( المطلق ) والأخص ( المطلق والأخص من وجه وصو به السيد السند ، وقال لاشك أنه كما يكون تصور الشيء بالكنه كيا محتاجا إلى التعريف كذلك تصوره بوجه ما سواء كان مع امتيازه عن جميع ما عداه أو عن بعضه فتصور المعرف بوجه أعم أو بوجه أخص يبيان أفراده المشهورة ) كقولك الإنسان حيوان ناطق ) والحيوان جسم نام حساس متحرك بالإرادة ، وكقولك الخفاش طائر ولود فتبصر . واعلم أن المشهور وجوب تقديم الجزء العام من التعريف على جزئه الخاص. وقيل لا يجب إلا إذا كان التعريف حدا تاما . وقيل لا يجب مطلقا وهو الأصح .
He said in Sharh al-Mawaqif: Equality is a condition for the complete definition, whether hadd or rasm, not for other [incomplete ones]. [It is] by the absolute broader and the absolute narrower and the narrower from one aspect, and al-Sayyid al-Sanad approved it. And he said: There is no doubt that just as the conceptualization of a thing as it is in itself, if acquired, needs a definition, so too its conceptualization in some respect, whether it involves distinction from all others or from some of them. So the conceptualization of the defined by a broader respect or a narrower respect to clarify its well-known individuals, as your saying: 'Man is a rational animal', and animal is a growing, sensing, volitionally-moving body, and as your saying: 'The bat is a flying mammal', so reflect. And know that the well-known [view] is the obligation of presenting the general part of the definition before its specific part. And it was said: It is not obligatory unless the definition is a complete hadd. And it was said: It is not obligatory at all, and this is the most correct.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage discusses the permissibility of using broader (a'amm) or narrower (akhass) terms in definitions. It begins by quoting Sharh al-Mawaqif, which states that equality (musawat) is a condition for complete definitions, but it is permissible to define using broader or narrower terms when the goal is to distinguish the defined from some, not all, things. This view is supported by al-Sayyid al-Sanad. The passage then gives examples: defining 'man' as 'rational animal' (a broader term 'animal' plus differentia), and defining 'bat' as 'flying mammal' (a narrower term 'mammal' and an accident 'flying'). Finally, it discusses the order of parts in a definition: the common view is that the broader (genus) should precede the specific (differentia), but some say this is only required for complete hadd, while the most correct view is that it is not obligatory at all. The passage thus shows flexibility in definitional practice.

الأخص المطلق
الأعم من وجه

Key Takeaway
Definitions need not always be coextensive; broader or narrower terms are acceptable when only partial distinction is needed.

Haqiqi vs Ismi Definitions and the Eight Types
Author distinguishes haqiqi from ismi definitions and classifies definitions into eight types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between haqiqi and ismi definitions and identify the eight types of definition according to the author.

Core Idea
Real definitions require existence; nominal definitions only concepts.

In this passage, the author draws a critical line between definitions that capture the essence of a thing (haqiqi) and those that merely capture its concept (ismi). He then shows how each can be either investigative or reminder, yielding an eightfold classification. Understanding this taxonomy is essential for precise concept formation in Islamic logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary distinction
Note that the author first divides definitions into haqiqi (real) and ismi (nominal). A haqiqi definition details the reality of the defined; an ismi definition details its concept. This is the foundational split.
2
Understand the existential condition
Observe that haqiqi definitions require the defined to exist in reality, because reality pertains to existents. Ismi definitions do not require existence; they can define non-existent entities (like a phoenix) since concepts are independent of existence.
3
Recognize the subtlety about 'haqiqi'
The author warns that 'haqiqi' here (opposed to ismi) is more specific than 'haqiqi' opposed to lafzi (verbal). Do not confuse them. This haqiqi is only one type of real definition.
4
Add the secondary distinction: tahqiqi vs tanbihi
Both haqiqi and ismi definitions can be tahqiqi (investigative, creating a new image) or tanbihi (reminder, recalling an existing image). This gives four types from the combination.
5
Derive the eight types
The author mentions 'mufrad' (single) at the start, indicating a third division: single vs composite. Combining haqiqi/ismi, tahqiqi/tanbihi, and mufrad/murakkab yields 2 × 2 × 2 = 8 types. All eight belong to concepts (tasawwurat).
The text explicitly says 'eight' and lists all as tasawwuri. The single/composite division is implied by the mention of 'single real definition'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما التعريف الحقيق المفرد عند من يجوزه فهو مفرد يراد به امتیاز المعرف عما عداه . والتعريف الحقيقى يسمى تعريفا حقيقيا إذا كان التفصيل والأمتياز تفصيل حقيقة المعرف أو امتيازها ، وتعريفا اسميا إذا كان تفصيل مفهوم المعرف وامتيازه والمعرف الاسمى يجوز أن يكون موجودا ومعدوما لأن المفهوم لا اختصاص له بالموجود بخلاف الحقيقى فان معرفه لا يكون إلا موجودا لأن الحقيقة مختصة بالموجودات وهذا الحقيق أى المقابل للاسمي، أخص من التعريف الحقيقي المقابل للتعريف اللفظى، فلا ينتقض التقسيم بانقسام الشيء إلى نفسه وإلى غيره وكل من الحقيقى والاسمى يسمى تعريفا تحقيقيا إن كان الغرض منه تحصيل صورة غير حاصلة ، وتنيها إن كان إحضار صورة مخزونة في الذهن كما سبق الإشارة إليه ، فمجموع هذه الأقسام ثمانية كلها من قبيل التصورات ؛ وإنما المراد من ذكر معرفها أن يتوجه ذهن المخاطب توجها إجماليا إلى ما يراد تفصيله وامتيازه لا حمل التعريف عليه وحمله صورى . نعم قد يقع التعريف مدعى أو مقدمة فحينئذ يكون تصديقا بلاشبهة ، وما قيل إن هذا التعريف التنبيهي من قبيل التصديقات فيأباه العقل السليم . وأما التعريف اللفظي فمن قبيل التصديقات لأن الغرض منه إفادة حال اللفظ بأنه موضوع لذلك المعنى لا بتصوير معنى اللفظ وإلا يكون تعريفا إسميا
As for the single real definition according to those who permit it, it is a single term by which is intended the distinction of the defined from other than it. And the real definition is called 'real' if the detail and distinction are a detailing of the reality of the defined or its distinction, and 'nominal' if it is a detailing and distinction of the concept of the defined. And the nominal defined can be existent or non-existent because the concept is not specific to the existent, unlike the real, for its defined is only existent because reality is specific to existents. And this 'real' meaning the opposite of 'nominal' is more specific than the real definition opposite to verbal definition, so the division is not invalidated by the division of a thing into itself and other. And both the real and nominal are called 'investigative' definition if the purpose is to acquire an image not yet obtained, and 'reminder' if it is to bring to mind an image stored in the mind, as previously indicated. So all these divisions are eight, all belonging to the category of concepts. But the purpose of mentioning their definitions is only to direct the mind of the addressee in a general way towards what is to be detailed and distinguished, not to impose the definition upon it; its imposition is figurative. Yes, the definition may occur as a claim or a premise, then it is a judgment without doubt. And what is said that this reminder definition is of the type of judgments, sound reason rejects it. As for the verbal definition, it is of the type of judgments because its purpose is to convey the state of the word, that it is assigned to that meaning, not to depict the meaning of the word; otherwise it would be a nominal definition.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage distinguishes between real (haqiqi) and nominal (ismi) definitions. A real definition details the essence or reality of the defined, while a nominal definition details only the concept. The nominal defined can be non-existent because concepts are not tied to existence, unlike real definitions which only apply to existent realities. The author notes that this 'real' (opposed to nominal) is more specific than the 'real definition' opposed to 'verbal definition'. Both real and nominal can be further divided into tahqiqi (investigative: acquiring a new concept) and tanbihi (reminder: recalling a stored concept), yielding eight types in total, all belonging to concepts (tasawwurat). The purpose of mentioning these definitions is to direct the listener's mind generally, not to strictly impose the definition. If a definition occurs as a claim or premise, it becomes a judgment (tasdiq). The author rejects the idea that reminder definitions are judgments. Verbal definitions are judgments because they explain the word's usage, not its meaning (that would be nominal). This classification shows the rich taxonomy of definitions in Islamic logic.

Key Terms
التعريف الحقيقي
التعريف الاسمي
تعريف تحقيقى
تعريف تنبيهي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, a nominal definition (ismi) differs from a real definition (haqiqi) in that:
A) It only applies to existent things
B) It can apply to non-existent things
C) It always includes a differentia
D) It is always a single term

Key Takeaway
Definitions in Islamic logic are classified by whether they capture reality or concept, and by their purpose (new or reminded image), yielding eight conceptual types.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Construct a haqiqi definition for 'zakat' (obligatory charity) that includes its reality (e.g., a specific portion of wealth given to specific categories), then contrast it with an ismi definition that only gives its concept.

Denying Premises in Definition Challenges
Author explains dialectical defense of definitions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the dialectical strategy of denying either the major or minor premise when a definition is challenged for lacking comprehensiveness or exclusiveness.

Core Idea
Definitions can be defended by denying their intended scope, not their logical form.

When a definition is attacked for not being comprehensive or exclusive, the defender has a powerful dialectical tool: deny the premise that all incomplete definitions are invalid. This passage from al-Waladiyya teaches how to distinguish between real and metaphorical definitions, and how to shift the burden of proof by focusing on the definition's purpose.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the two premises of the objection
The opponent uses a syllogism: major premise 'Every definition that is not comprehensive/exclusive is invalid', minor premise 'This definition is not comprehensive/exclusive'. Identify both premises.
2
Assess the intended purpose of the definition
Determine whether the definition is meant to be real (haqiqi) or metaphorical (majazi). Real definitions require full comprehensiveness and exclusiveness; metaphorical definitions aim to distinguish from some things or list well-known individuals.
3
Choose your denial strategy
If the definition is metaphorical, deny the major premise by arguing that the purpose is limited. If the definition is real, you may need to deny the minor premise by redefining the defined term.
The passage also mentions a command 'tafattan' (be attentive), indicating nuances in the applicability of these strategies.
4
Articulate the denial with proper basis
Provide a basis (sana) for your denial, e.g., 'This definition is based on the doctrine of earlier scholars who allow definitions that are not fully comprehensive.' This grounds your denial in established scholarly views.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
منع الكبرى أيضا منعا مستندا بسند أخص بأن المراد من التعريف تميز المعرف عن بعض الأشياء إذا كان التعريف أعم مطلقا أو من وجه أو بيان الأفراد المشهورة إذا كان التعريف أخص مطلقا أو من وجه تفطن فتح الله بتوهم اشتراط المساواة عندهم أيضا، وبأن الجواب تحقيقي لا جدلى ، ويحتمل أن يكون وجه التفطن أن صاحب التعريف إنما يمنع الكبرى إذا كان تصوير النقض ما قرره . وأما إذا قرر بأن هذا التعريف مباين للعرف فيكون فاسدا فلا مجال لمنع الكبرى بل يمنع الصغرى مستندا بتحرير المعرف أو التعريف .. ويحتمل أن يكون وجهه أن دليل النقض كما يقبل المنع كذلك يقبل النقض والمعارضة فالاكتفاء مبنى على التمثيل أو على الأغلب عن بعض الأشياء المغايرة له أو بيان المعرف بتعريف أفراده المشهورة وتميزه عن جميع الأغيار أو بيان المعرف بتعريف أفراده المشهورة وتمييزه عن بعض الأغيار الأول للثاني والثاني للأول والثالث لكل منهما . أقول: المفهوم من كتب القوم أنه لا نزاع بينهم في بيان الشيء بالأعم مطلقا أو من وجه إذا كان الغرض من بيانه امتيازه عن بعض ما عداه ولا في بيانه بالأخص مطلقا إذا كان الغرض من بیانه بیان بعض الأفراد كما صرح به بعض الأفاضل ولعل النزاع فى التسمية فإن المحققين من المتقدمين يسمون كلا من تلك البيانات تعريفا دون المتأخرين وبعض من المتقدمين فإنهم يسمونها لواحق التعريف ويطلقون اسم التعريف عليها مجازا فلصاحب التعريف أن يردد ويقول إن أردت بقولك أن تعريف كذا تعريف حقيقة كذاً فالصغرى مجموعة ، وإن أردت أنه تعريف مجازا لكذا فالكبرى أو تكرار الحد الأوسط ممنوع . ولعل لهذا أمر بقوله تفطن فتح الله عليك ويحتمل أن يكون إشارة إلى أن الكبرى إنما تقبل المنع إذا قرر النقض كما قررناه، وقلما يقر بأنه مباين للمعرف وكل تعريف هذا شأنه ففاسد فحينئذ لا مجال لمنع الكبرى بل يمنع الصغرى وسيجي، بيانه ولا يبعد أن يقال إنه إشارة إلى سؤال وجواب، تقرير السؤال أن هذا الدليل كما يقبل المنع كذلك يقبل النقض والمعارضة فالحصر المستفاد في معرض البيان ممنوع وتقرير الجواب لما كان عادة المناظرين ا . هنا المنع لاغير وإن لم يأبه العقل ولا الدليل جواز النقض والمعارضة اقتصرنا عليه فصل في بيان منع كل من الصغرى الأولى وهى أن هذا التعريف غير جامع لأفراد المعرف والثانية وهى أن التعريف غير مانع عن أغبار المعرف في التقرير السابق اعلم أن كلا من الصغرى الأولى والثانية فيه أي في التقرير السابق
Also denying the major premise, a denial based on a more specific basis: that the intended meaning of the definition is to distinguish the defined from some things if the definition is absolutely broader or from one aspect, or to explain the well-known individuals if the definition is absolutely narrower or from one aspect. Be attentive, O God, to the difficulties upon you. It is possible that the reason for the command to be attentive is that the answer does not match the question because it is based on the doctrine of the later scholars, while the answer is based on the doctrine of the earlier scholars, so there is no correspondence between them. And it can be refuted by saying that the question is also based on the doctrine of the earlier scholars under the illusion that they also required equality, and that the answer is investigative (tahqiqi) not dialectical (jadali). And it is possible that the reason for being attentive is that the holder of the definition only denies the major premise if the depiction of the refutation (naqd) is as he stated. But if it is stated that this definition is opposed to the conventional meaning, then it is invalid, so there is no room to deny the major premise; rather, he denies the minor premise based on redefining the defined or the definition. And it is possible that its reason is that the proof of refutation, just as it admits denial, also admits refutation and contradiction, so the limitation is based on example or on the most common. Chapter on explaining the denial of the minor premise or one of them, which is that this definition is not comprehensive or not exclusive, so it includes the two minor premises in the previous formulation. And when that explanation needed detail, he attended to it and presented it in a separate chapter, so he said: Know that the minor premise absolutely—meaning in the previous formulation—is the denial of the universality of the major premise established, which is: every definition that is not comprehensive or not exclusive is invalid—based on the fact that this definition is built upon the doctrine of the verifiers among the earlier scholars: its intended meaning is to distinguish the defined with all its individuals from some things different from it, or to explain the defined by defining its well-known individuals and distinguishing it from all others, or to explain the defined by defining its well-known individuals and distinguishing it from some others. The first is for the second, the second for the first, and the third for both. I say: it is understood from the books of the people that there is no dispute among them regarding explaining a thing by the absolutely broader or from one aspect if the purpose of its explanation is its distinction from some things other than it, nor regarding explaining it by the absolutely narrower if the purpose of its explanation is to explain some individuals, as some virtuous scholars have stated. Perhaps the dispute is about terminology: the verifiers among the earlier scholars call each of these explanations a definition, unlike the later scholars and some of the earlier scholars who call them adjuncts to definition (lawaḥiq al-ta'rif) and apply the name 'definition' to them metaphorically. So the holder of the definition can alternate and say: If by your statement 'this definition is a definition of such-and-such' you mean a real definition, then the minor premise is conceded; and if you mean it is a metaphorical definition of such-and-such, then the major premise is denied, or the repetition of the middle term is denied. Perhaps for this reason He commanded His statement: 'Be attentive, O God, to you.' And it is possible that it is an indication that the major premise only admits denial if the refutation is stated as we stated it. And rarely does he state that it is opposed to the defined, and any definition with this characteristic is invalid; then there is no room to deny the major premise, but rather he denies the minor premise, and its explanation will come. And it is not far that it is said that it is an indication of a question and answer: the formulation of the question is that this proof, just as it admits denial, also admits refutation and contradiction, so the limitation derived in the context of explanation is denied; and the formulation of the answer is: since the habit of the disputants is that only denial is used here—even if reason and proof do not mind the permissibility of refutation and contradiction—we restrict ourselves to it. Chapter on explaining the denial of each of the first minor premise—which is that this definition is not comprehensive of the individuals of the defined—and the second—which is that the definition is not exclusive of the others of the defined—in the previous formulation. Know that each of the first and second minor premises is in it, i.e., in the previous formulation.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage is a dialectical explanation of how to respond when a definition is criticized for lacking comprehensiveness (jami') or exclusiveness (mani'). It begins by discussing the denial of the major premise (kubra) which states that 'every definition that is not comprehensive or exclusive is invalid'. The defender can deny this by arguing that the definition's purpose is limited: either to distinguish from some things (if broader) or to mention well-known individuals (if narrower). The author then notes a command to be attentive ('tafattan'), offering three interpretations: (1) The answer is based on earlier scholars' views while the question assumes later scholars' views, causing mismatch, but this can be rebutted; (2) The denial of the major premise is only valid if the refutation (naqd) is framed in a certain way; if the refutation claims the definition is opposed to convention, the defender must deny the minor premise (sughra) instead; (3) The proof of refutation can itself be refuted or contradicted, so limiting to denial is based on convention.  The text then transitions to a new chapter specifically on denying the minor premise(s). The minor premises are two: that the definition is not comprehensive and that it is not exclusive. The defender can claim that the definition follows the doctrine of early verifiers, where definition can be for limited distinction or explaining well-known individuals. The author clarifies that there is no dispute among scholars on the permissibility of such definitions when the purpose is limited; the dispute is merely terminological—whether to call them 'definition' (ta'rif) or 'adjuncts to definition' (lawaḥiq al-ta'rif). Consequently, the defender can argue that if the opponent intends a real definition, the minor premise (that it is not comprehensive/exclusive) is conceded; but if the opponent intends a metaphorical definition, the major premise (that every such definition is invalid) is denied. The passage ends with a note that in dialectical practice, only denial (man') is commonly used, ignoring other possible objections like refutation or contradiction, due to convention. Overall, this passage teaches the subtle art of responding to definitional challenges by identifying the intended scope of the definition and leveraging terminological ambiguities.

Identifying Impossible Circularity in Definitions
Explains two types of circularity and their impossibility conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between possible and impossible circularity (dawr) in definitions and identify whether a given definition contains an impossible circularity.

Core Idea
Simultaneous circularity is only impossible when it occurs between definiens and definiendum.

In this lesson, we explore the types of circularity that can invalidate a definition. The author explains that not all circularities are logically problematic; only those that affect the definiens-definiendum relationship are forbidden. We will learn to recognize both simultaneous (dawr ma'i) and sequential (dawr taqaddumi) circularity and determine which are impossible.

Guided Path
1
Identify definiens and definiendum
Locate the term being defined and the words used to define it. For example, in 'father is one who has a son', 'father' is the definiendum and 'one who has a son' is the definiens.
2
Check for mutual dependence
Does the definiens rely on the definiendum and vice versa? If yes, this is simultaneous circularity (dawr ma'i). Evaluate whether this occurs directly between the definition and the defined term.
If the dependence is indirect (through a chain), it is sequential circularity (dawr taqaddumi).
3
Apply impossibility condition
For dawr ma'i, impossibility only arises when the circle is between the definiens and definiendum. For dawr taqaddumi, any sequential circle makes the definition impossible.
Al-Taftazani's rule: 'One of two correlatives cannot be taken in the definition of the other, because the definition must be understood before the defined.'
4
Test with an example
Consider the definition 'quality is that by which similarity and dissimilarity occur'. Then 'similarity is agreement in quality'. Is there circularity? Trace the dependence.

Source Text

أو يمنع الاستحالة ( سواء كان قيدا كما في التقرير الأول أو كبرى كما في التقرير الثاني أو يمنع الاستحالة والاستلزام معا لكن على تقدير التسليم بأن يقال لا نسلم أنه يستلزم الدور أو التسلسل وإن سلم أنه مستلزم لأحدها فلا نسلم أنه دور محال أو تسلسل محال فظهر أن كلمة أو لمنع الخلو منعا (مستندا بأن هذا الدور غير محال ) لأنه دور معي بين أجزاء التعريف (أو) أن هذا التسلسل غير محال لأنه تسلسل في الأمور الاعتبارية أو فى الأمور المعدة ، ولا يخفى أن هذا تصوير للمنع لاسنده كما لا يخفى على من تتبع مناظرات المؤلفين ، اللهم إلا أن يقال إنه سماد مندا مسامحة لكونه توطئة للسند كما أشرنا إليه ) وبيان محالها (
