الشمسية : أحد المتضايفين لا يجوز أخذه في تعريف الآخر، لأن الحد يجب أن يعقل قبل المحدود، والمتضايفان يكون تعلقهما معا. وأما الدور التقدمي فهو توقف الشيء على ما يتوقف عليه بمرتبة أو بمراتب وهو إما مصرح أو مضمر . أما المصرح فكتعريف الكيفية بمايقع به للمشابهة واللامشابهة والمشابهة اتفاق في الكيفية . وأما المضمر فكما يقال الاثنان الزوج الأول، ثم يقال الزوج الأول هو للنقم بمتساويين ، ثم يقال المتساويان هما الشيئان اللذان لا يفضل أحدهما عن الآخر ، ثم بقاله الشيئان الاثنان، وأن التسلسل ترتيب أمور غير متناهية ، وهو إما في جانب العلل إن أخذ العلول أولاء واستفسر عن العلة أو فى جانب المعلول إن أخذ بالعكس وكل منهما محال عند المتكامين بل حكموا باستحالة مطلق الأمور الغير المتناهية سواء كانت مرتبة أولا وسواء كانت مجتمعة في الوجود أولا . وأما الحكماء فاشترطوا في استحالته أمورا ثلاثة كون الأمور مجتمعة وموجودة ومرتبة لأن جريان برهان التطبيق والتضايف بل البرهان العرشى أيضا موقوف عليها فتبطله . فإذا انتفى أحد الأمور بأن لم تكن الأمور موجودة كما بين المعلومات أو كانت موجودة ولم تكن مجتمعة كما بين المعدات أو كانت مجمعة ولم تسكن مرتبة كما بين النفوس الناطقة لم يكن محالا عندهم كما هو المشهور ( ويكفيك هنا هذا الإجمال ) أو يمنع الاستحالة مستندا بأن هذا الدور غير محال لكونه دورا متعينا بين أجزاء التعريف وأن هذا التسلسل غير محال في الأمور الاعتيادية أو في المعدات، ويجوز أن يكون وهو محال كبرى فيكون القياس قياسا مركبا مفصول النتيجة من قياسين متعارف أو غير متعارف فمنع الاستحالة حينئذ منع الكبرى ، وقد لا يكون فى التقرير قيد المحالية فاصاحب التعريف حينئذ أن يمنع الصغرى وكلية الكبرى، وقد يردد ويقول إن أردت أنه مستلزم للدور أو التسلسل المحال فالصغرى ممنوعة وإن أردت أنه مستلزم للدور أو التسلسل مطلقا فكلية الكبرى ممنوعة والأسانيد معلومة مما تقدم وبيان محالهما ( أى بيان ما كان محالا من الدور والتسلسل ) عن عدم محالها ( أى عما لا يكون منهما لميين ( في علم الكلام ، ويكفيك هذا الإجمال هنا ) إذ لكل مقام مقال، ولكل ميدان رجاله
Or he prevents impossibility, whether it is a restriction as in the first report or a major premise as in the second report, or he prevents both impossibility and entailment together, but on condition of admission by saying: we do not accept that it entails circularity or infinite regress, and even if it is accepted that it entails one of them, we do not accept that it is an impossible circularity or an impossible infinite regress. So it appears that the word 'or' is for preventing vacuity, based on the claim that this circularity is not impossible because it is simultaneous circularity between parts of the definition, or that this infinite regress is not impossible because it is a regress in mental matters or in potential things. And it is not hidden that this is a depiction of prevention without its basis, as is not hidden on those who follow the debates of the authors, unless it is said that it is a basis by way of approximation because it is a preparation for the basis as we indicated. And explanation of their impossibility, i.e., distinguishing the impossible kind of circularity and infinite regress from their non-impossibility, i.e., the kind that is not impossible for them, in theology, i.e., in the science of belief. Know that circularity is either simultaneous or sequential. As for simultaneous circularity, it is the thing being with another like correlatives. For the occurrence of each of them in the mind entails the occurrence of the other in it together without one preceding the other, and it is not impossible except when it occurs between the definiendum and the definiens, like defining father by one who has a son. Al-Muhaqqiq al-Taftazani said in Sharh al-Shamsiyya: One of the two correlatives may not be taken in the definition of the other, because the definition must be understood before the definiendum, and the two correlatives have their relation together. As for sequential circularity, it is the dependence of a thing on what it depends on by one degree or degrees, and it is either explicit or implicit. As for explicit, like defining quality by that by which similarity and dissimilarity occur, and similarity is agreement in quality. As for implicit, like it is said: two is the first even number, then it is said: the first even number is a number divisible into two equal parts, then it is said: two equal parts are two things neither of which exceeds the other, then it is said: two things are two. And that infinite regress is an arrangement of infinite things, and it is either on the side of causes if the effect is taken first and one asks about the cause, or on the side of the effect if taken in reverse, and each of them is impossible according to the theologians, indeed they rule on the impossibility of absolute infinite things whether ordered or not, and whether simultaneous in existence or not. As for the philosophers, they stipulate for its impossibility three things: that the things be simultaneous, existent, and ordered because the validity of the proof of correspondence and correlation, indeed the Throne proof, depends on them; if they are invalidated, then if one of the conditions is absent, such as the things not being existent as in the case of bits of knowledge, or they are existent but not simultaneous as in the case of potential things, or they are simultaneous but not ordered as in the case of rational souls, then it is not impossible according to them, as is well-known. And this summary suffices here. Or he prevents impossibility based on the claim that this circularity is not impossible because it is simultaneous circularity between parts of the definition, and that this infinite regress is not impossible in conventional matters or in potential things. And it is possible that it is an impossible major premise, then the syllogism becomes a compound syllogism with the conclusion separated from two conventional or unconventional syllogisms; then prevention of impossibility here is prevention of the major premise. And sometimes the report does not have the restriction of impossibility, so the definer then may deny the minor premise or the universality of the major premise. And he may alternate and say: if you mean that it entails impossible circularity or infinite regress, then the minor premise is denied; if you mean that it entails circularity or infinite regress absolutely, then the universality of the major premise is denied. The grounds are known from what preceded. And explanation of what is impossible of them (i.e., explanation of what is impossible from circularity and infinite regress) from their non-impossibility (i.e., from what is not from them of the two kinds) in theology, and this summary suffices here, for every station has its discourse, and every field has its men.
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage deals with the objection of impossibility (man' al-istihala) in definitions, specifically when a definition is attacked for leading to circularity (dawr) or infinite regress (tasalsul). The author explains how the definer (sahib al-ta'rif) can respond by denying the impossibility. The text first discusses the two possibilities: either the definition entails a circle or a regress. The definer may accept the entailment but deny that the circle or regress is impossible. The author clarifies that the word 'or' in the objection is meant to prevent vacuity (man' al-khulu); the definer can argue that the circle is not impossible because it is a simultaneous circle (dawr ma'i) between parts of the definition, and such simultaneous circles are not inherently impossible except when between definiens and definiendum. Similarly, the regress may be in mental or potential matters, which are not impossible. The author then provides a detailed exposition of the two types of circularity and infinite regress. Simultaneous circularity (dawr ma'i) is exemplified by correlatives like father and son; it is impossible only between definiens and definiendum because the definition must be known before the defined. Sequential circularity (dawr taqaddumi) involves a chain of dependencies, either explicit or implicit. Infinite regress (tasalsul) is an arrangement of infinite terms; theologians consider all infinite regress impossible, while philosophers stipulate three conditions (simultaneity, existence, order) for impossibility. The author then returns to the definer's strategy: depending on how the objection is framed, the definer may deny the minor premise (that the definition leads to a circle/regress) or the universality of the major premise (that all circles/regresses are impossible). The lesson concludes by emphasizing that detailed explanation is left to theology, as each discipline has its own scope.

Conditions for Impossible Infinite Regress
Explains the conditions for impossible infinite regress and the difference between theologians and philosophers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the three conditions that philosophers require for an infinite regress to be impossible, and contrast this with the theologians' absolute rejection.

Core Idea
Theologians reject all infinite regress; philosophers allow it unless the series is simultaneous, existent, and ordered.

Infinite regress (tasalsul) is another objection to definitions. The author explains that there is disagreement between theologians (mutakallimun) and philosophers (hukama') on when regress is impossible. We will examine the three conditions of impossibility according to the philosophers and see how this applies to definition and broader theological arguments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the regress in a definition
Determine whether the definition leads to an infinite chain of dependencies. For example, if each term in the definition refers to another term that itself requires definition, an infinite regress may occur.
2
Classify the regress type
Is the regress in the side of causes (taking the effect first and asking for its cause) or effects (taking the cause first and asking for its effect)? This matters for the philosophers' conditions.
3
Apply the three conditions of impossibility
Philosophers say regress is impossible only when the chain is simultaneous (all terms exist together), existent (real, not mental), and ordered (has a direction). Theologians reject all regress regardless.
Examples: bits of knowledge are not simultaneous; potential things are not existent; rational souls are simultaneous but not ordered.
4
Evaluate the definition
If the regress fails any condition, it is not impossible per philosophers. Decide whether the definition is acceptable or not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

مستلزم لأحدها فلا نسلم أنه دور محال أو تسلسل محال فظهر أن كلمة أو لمنع الخلو منعا (مستندا بأن هذا الدور غير محال ) لأنه دور معي بين أجزاء التعريف (أو) أن هذا التسلسل غير محال لأنه تسلسل في الأمور أى تمييز القسم المحال من الدور والتسلسل ( عن عدم محالها ( أى عن القسم الغير المحال لهما ( في علم الكلام ) أي في علم القائد. اعلم أن الدور إما معى أو تقدمى . أما الدور المعى فهو كون الشيء مع الآخر كالمتضايفين . فان حصول كل منهما في المفكرة يستلزم حصول الآخر فيها معا بلا تقدم من أحدهما على الآخر وهو ليس بمحال إلا أن يقع بين المعرف والتعريف كتعريف الأب بمن له ابن . قال المحقق التفتازاني في شرح أو مضمر . أما المصرح فكتعريف الكيفية بمايقع به للمشابهة واللامشابهة والمشابهة اتفاق في الكيفية . وأما المضمر فكما يقال الاثنان الزوج الأول، ثم يقال الزوج الأول هو للنقم بمتساويين ، ثم يقال المتساويان هما الشيئان اللذان لا يفضل أحدهما عن الآخر ، ثم بقاله الشيئان الاثنان، وأن التسلسل ترتيب أمور غير متناهية ، وهو إما في جانب العلل إن أخذ العلول أولاء واستفسر عن العلة أو فى جانب المعلول إن أخذ بالعكس وكل منهما محال عند المتكامين بل حكموا باستحالة مطلق الأمور الغير المتناهية سواء كانت مرتبة أولا وسواء كانت مجتمعة في الوجود أولا . وأما الحكماء فاشترطوا في استحالته أمورا ثلاثة كون الأمور مجتمعة وموجودة ومرتبة لأن جريان برهان التطبيق والتضايف بل البرهان العرشى أيضا موقوف عليها فتبطله . فإذا انتفى أحد الأمور بأن لم تكن الأمور موجودة كما بين المعلومات أو كانت موجودة ولم تكن مجتمعة كما بين المعدات أو كانت مجمعة ولم تسكن مرتبة كما بين النفوس الناطقة لم يكن محالا عندهم كما هو المشهور ( ويكفيك هنا هذا الإجمال ) أو يمنع الاستحالة مستندا بأن هذا الدور غير محال لكونه دورا متعينا بين أجزاء التعريف وأن هذا التسلسل غير محال في الأمور الاعتيادية أو في المعدات، ويجوز أن يكون وهو محال كبرى فيكون القياس قياسا مركبا مفصول النتيجة من قياسين متعارف أو غير متعارف فمنع الاستحالة حينئذ منع الكبرى ، وقد لا يكون فى التقرير قيد المحالية فاصاحب التعريف حينئذ أن يمنع الصغرى وكلية الكبرى، وقد يردد ويقول إن أردت أنه مستلزم للدور أو التسلسل المحال فالصغرى ممنوعة وإن أردت أنه مستلزم للدور أو التسلسل مطلقا فكلية الكبرى ممنوعة والأسانيد معلومة مما تقدم وبيان محالهما ( أى بيان ما كان محالا من الدور والتسلسل ) عن عدم محالها ( أى عما لا يكون منهما لميين ( في علم الكلام ، ويكفيك هذا الإجمال هنا ) إذ لكل مقام مقال، ولكل ميدان رجاله
Or he prevents impossibility, whether it is a restriction as in the first report or a major premise as in the second report, or he prevents both impossibility and entailment together, but on condition of admission by saying: we do not accept that it entails circularity or infinite regress, and even if it is accepted that it entails one of them, we do not accept that it is an impossible circularity or an impossible infinite regress. So it appears that the word 'or' is for preventing vacuity, based on the claim that this circularity is not impossible because it is simultaneous circularity between parts of the definition, or that this infinite regress is not impossible because it is a regress in mental matters or in potential things. And it is not hidden that this is a depiction of prevention without its basis, as is not hidden on those who follow the debates of the authors, unless it is said that it is a basis by way of approximation because it is a preparation for the basis as we indicated. And explanation of their impossibility, i.e., distinguishing the impossible kind of circularity and infinite regress from their non-impossibility, i.e., the kind that is not impossible for them, in theology, i.e., in the science of belief. Know that circularity is either simultaneous or sequential. As for simultaneous circularity, it is the thing being with another like correlatives. For the occurrence of each of them in the mind entails the occurrence of the other in it together without one preceding the other, and it is not impossible except when it occurs between the definiendum and the definiens, like defining father by one who has a son. Al-Muhaqqiq al-Taftazani said in Sharh al-Shamsiyya: One of the two correlatives may not be taken in the definition of the other, because the definition must be understood before the definiendum, and the two correlatives have their relation together. As for sequential circularity, it is the dependence of a thing on what it depends on by one degree or degrees, and it is either explicit or implicit. As for explicit, like defining quality by that by which similarity and dissimilarity occur, and similarity is agreement in quality. As for implicit, like it is said: two is the first even number, then it is said: the first even number is a number divisible into two equal parts, then it is said: two equal parts are two things neither of which exceeds the other, then it is said: two things are two. And that infinite regress is an arrangement of infinite things, and it is either on the side of causes if the effect is taken first and one asks about the cause, or on the side of the effect if taken in reverse, and each of them is impossible according to the theologians, indeed they rule on the impossibility of absolute infinite things whether ordered or not, and whether simultaneous in existence or not. As for the philosophers, they stipulate for its impossibility three things: that the things be simultaneous, existent, and ordered because the validity of the proof of correspondence and correlation, indeed the Throne proof, depends on them; if they are invalidated, then if one of the conditions is absent, such as the things not being existent as in the case of bits of knowledge, or they are existent but not simultaneous as in the case of potential things, or they are simultaneous but not ordered as in the case of rational souls, then it is not impossible according to them, as is well-known. And this summary suffices here. Or he prevents impossibility based on the claim that this circularity is not impossible because it is simultaneous circularity between parts of the definition, and that this infinite regress is not impossible in conventional matters or in potential things. And it is possible that it is an impossible major premise, then the syllogism becomes a compound syllogism with the conclusion separated from two conventional or unconventional syllogisms; then prevention of impossibility here is prevention of the major premise. And sometimes the report does not have the restriction of impossibility, so the definer then may deny the minor premise or the universality of the major premise. And he may alternate and say: if you mean that it entails impossible circularity or infinite regress, then the minor premise is denied; if you mean that it entails circularity or infinite regress absolutely, then the universality of the major premise is denied. The grounds are known from what preceded. And explanation of what is impossible of them (i.e., explanation of what is impossible from circularity and infinite regress) from their non-impossibility (i.e., from what is not from them of the two kinds) in theology, and this summary suffices here, for every station has its discourse, and every field has its men.
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage deals with the objection of impossibility (man' al-istihala) in definitions, specifically when a definition is attacked for leading to circularity (dawr) or infinite regress (tasalsul). The author explains how the definer (sahib al-ta'rif) can respond by denying the impossibility. The text first discusses the two possibilities: either the definition entails a circle or a regress. The definer may accept the entailment but deny that the circle or regress is impossible. The author clarifies that the word 'or' in the objection is meant to prevent vacuity (man' al-khulu); the definer can argue that the circle is not impossible because it is a simultaneous circle (dawr ma'i) between parts of the definition, and such simultaneous circles are not inherently impossible except when between definiens and definiendum. Similarly, the regress may be in mental or potential matters, which are not impossible. The author then provides a detailed exposition of the two types of circularity and infinite regress. Simultaneous circularity (dawr ma'i) is exemplified by correlatives like father and son; it is impossible only between definiens and definiendum because the definition must be known before the defined. Sequential circularity (dawr taqaddumi) involves a chain of dependencies, either explicit or implicit. Infinite regress (tasalsul) is an arrangement of infinite terms; theologians consider all infinite regress impossible, while philosophers stipulate three conditions (simultaneity, existence, order) for impossibility. The author then returns to the definer's strategy: depending on how the objection is framed, the definer may deny the minor premise (that the definition leads to a circle/regress) or the universality of the major premise (that all circles/regresses are impossible). The lesson concludes by emphasizing that detailed explanation is left to theology, as each discipline has its own scope.

Key Terms
التسلسل
المتكلمون
الحكماء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) When it is a regress in mental matters (bits of knowledge)
B) When the series is simultaneous, existent, and ordered
C) When it is a regress in potential things (instruments)
D) Always, without exception

Key Takeaway
Philosophers allow infinite regress unless the series is simultaneous, existent, and ordered; theologians reject all regress.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

If one then defines 'belief' as 'an acceptance that something is true', and 'acceptance' as 'a mental state that leads to belief', does this create an infinite regress? Apply the three conditions to determine if it is impossible per philosophers.

The Definition Must Be Clearer Than the Defined
Author enlists violations of the clarity condition for definitions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify violations of the clarity condition in definitions and explain why they fail.

Core Idea
A definition that is not clearer than the defined is no definition at all.

This passage from the matn establishes a fundamental condition for any valid definition: the definiens must be clearer (ajla) than the definiendum. The author outlines three types of violations: equal clarity, greater obscurity, and circularity. Understanding this condition is essential for evaluating the quality of definitions in any Islamic science.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central condition for definitions
Find the key phrase in the Arabic: 'ليس بأجلى من المعرف' (not clearer than the defined). The author states that any definition that is not clearer is corrupt.
This is the core condition: the definition must be more evident than the term it defines.
2
Recognize the first violation: equal clarity
The example of correlatives (mutadāyifān): defining 'father' as 'one who has a son'. Both terms are equally known only in relation to each other, so the definition does not increase understanding.
This violation is not circular but fails to clarify because of interdependence.
3
Recognize the second violation: greater obscurity with circularity
The example of defining 'khabar' (statement) as 'that which admits truth and falsehood', when truth is itself defined as correspondence with reality. The definition depends on the concept of truth, which is defined in terms of statements, creating a circle.
This is a refutation by necessitating circularity (dawr).
4
Recognize the third violation: greater obscurity in meaning
The example of defining 'fire' as 'a thing resembling the soul (nafs) in subtlety and invisibility'. The definiens (soul) is even more obscure than the definiendum (fire). The gloss clarifies that fire here means the heat in embers, but the comparison fails to clarify.
The author remarks that the soul is more hidden than fire, so this definition is invalid.
5
Apply the condition to evaluate a definition
Given a definition from fiqh or kalam, check whether the definiens is clearer than the definiendum. For example, is defining 'riba' as 'excess without return' clearer than the term itself?
If the definiens is equally or more obscure, the definition is invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
( واعلم أنه قد ينقض التعريف ) الحقيقى ( بأنه ليس بأجلى من المعرف ) وكل تعريف هذا شأنه تفاسد ، وذلك إما بأن يكون المعرف والتعريف متساويين في المعرفة والجهالة ولكونهما متضايفين كتعريف الأب بمن له ولد ، وإما بأن يكون التعريف أخفى من المعرف لتوقف معرفته على معرفة المعرف كتعريف الخبر بما احتمل الصدق والكذب على تقدير كون الصدق مطابقة الخبر للواقع والكذب عدم مطابقته وهو المشهور والنقض بهذين نقض باستلزام الدور في الحقيقة فيدخل في النقض باستلزام المحال ، وإما بأن يكون أخفى من المعرف لكون معرفة معناه صعبا من معرفة مميز للعرف كتعريف النار بأنه والتذكير باعتبار الخبر (شيء يشبه النفس) بسكون الفاء (في اللطافة) وعدم الرؤية قال فى الحاشية والمراد من النار الحر السارى فى الجمر وقد طاق على الجمر و المراد هنا هو الأول انتهى. إذ لالطافة فى الجمر وقد قيل فى الحركة دائما فان النار متحركة بحركة دورية تبعا للفلك كما أن النفس متحركة بحركة تخييلية فعلى هذا المراد من السكرة النارية المماسة سطحها سطح فلك القمر فانها لطيفة غير مرئية متحركة على الاستدارة بحركة الفلك الأعظم وقبل في إحداث الحمة في مجاورها فان الماء المسخن بالنار أخف من الماء البارد كما أن الحى أخف من الميت وقيل في تسخين متعلقها فان الميت أبرد من الحى فعلى هذين مجوز أن يراد من النار كل واحد من الثلاثة فتأمل (أقول: والفس أخف من النار )
(And know that the definition) real definition (may be refuted by being not clearer than the defined). And every definition that is like this is corrupt. That is either because the defined and the definition are equal in knowledge and ignorance, due to them being correlatives, like defining father by one who has a son; or because the definition is more obscure than the defined, due to its knowledge being dependent on knowledge of the defined, like defining khabar (statement) by that which admits truth and falsehood, on the assumption that truth is correspondence of the statement with reality and falsehood is non-correspondence—which is the well-known definition—and refutation by these two is a refutation by necessitating circularity in reality, thus it enters the refutation by necessitating the impossible; or because the definition is more obscure than the defined due to the difficulty of understanding its meaning compared to understanding the characteristic of the term, like defining fire by that which, with the masculine pronoun considering the predicate, (is a thing resembling the soul) with sukun on the fa' (in subtlety) and invisibility. He said in the gloss: 'By fire is meant the heat that spreads in embers, and it is also applied to the ember itself, but here it is the first meaning.' End. For there is no subtlety in the ember. And it has been said in constant motion, for fire moves with a circular motion following the sphere, just as the soul moves with an imaginative motion. On this, what is meant is the fiery sphere whose surface touches the surface of the moon's sphere, for it is subtle, invisible, moving circularly with the motion of the supreme sphere. And it has been said in generating lightness in its surroundings, for water heated by fire is lighter than cold water, just as the living is lighter than the dead. And it has been said in heating its subject, for the dead is colder than the living. On these two, it is possible that by fire each of the three is meant, so reflect. I say: and the soul is more hidden than fire.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage enumerates the condition that a definition must be clearer (ajla) than the defined term (al-mu'arraf). The author states that any definition that is not clearer is corrupt (fasid). He then categorizes the violations into three types. First, the defined and the definition may be equal in clarity, as in correlatives (mutadāyifān) like defining 'father' as 'one who has a son'—both terms are equally known only in relation to each other, so the definition fails to clarify. Second, the definition may be more obscure than the defined because its understanding depends on understanding the defined, which leads to circularity; an example is defining 'statement' (khabar) as 'that which admits truth and falsehood' when truth is itself defined in terms of correspondence with reality—this is a common definition that suffers from circularity. Third, the definition may be more obscure than the defined simply because the meaning of the definiens is harder to grasp than the meaning of the defined term; the author gives the example of defining 'fire' as 'a thing resembling the soul (nafs) in subtlety and invisibility'. He then elaborates on this example, citing a gloss that clarifies 'fire' here means the heat that spreads in embers (al-harr al-sārī fī al-jamr), not the ember itself. The subtlety and invisibility of fire are likened to the soul, which is subtle and invisible. The author also mentions alternative interpretations: fire's constant circular motion, its lightness, or its heating effect. He concludes that the soul is even more hidden than fire, so this definition fails to clarify and is therefore invalid.

Key Terms
أجلى
المعرف
التعريف

Key Takeaway
A valid definition must be clearer than the defined; violations include equal clarity, circularity, and greater obscurity.

Condition of Definition Being Clearer Than Definiendum
Author explains the naqd of definition by lack of clarity with examples and proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and refute a definition that fails the condition of being clearer than the definiendum.

Core Idea
A definition must be clearer than what it defines; otherwise, it fails.

In this lesson, we explore a critical condition for a valid definition: it must be more evident (ajla) than the definiendum. The author explains three ways this condition can be violated, using examples like father-son correlatives, circular definitions of report, and obscure descriptions of fire. Understanding this condition helps you evaluate whether a definition actually clarifies or obscures.

Guided Path
1
Understand the clarity condition
A valid definition must be clearer (ajla) than the definiendum. This means the definition should be more easily understood or more evident than the term it defines.
Clarity is relative, not absolute.
2
Identify the three violation types
The author lists three ways a definition can fail: (1) equal clarity due to correlatives (e.g., father/son), (2) definition more obscure because it depends on the definiendum (circular), (3) definition more obscure due to inherent difficulty (e.g., defining fire by soul).
Each type shows the definition does not clarify.
3
Reconstruct the logical argument
The author provides a conditional argument: if a definition is not clearer, it is invalid. For the fire example, the minor premise is 'this definition is not clearer because it uses the soul, which is more obscure.' The major premise is the condition itself. The conclusion follows by modus ponens.
The major premise is the condition; the minor premise is the specific failure.
4
Apply the condition to a new definition
Take a definition from Islamic sciences and test it: e.g., define 'qiyas' as 'applying a ruling from an original case to a new case due to a shared effective cause.' Is this clearer than 'qiyas'? If not, it fails.
Ensure the definition does not rely on terms equally or more obscure.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أنه قد ينقض التعريف الحقيقي بأنه ليس بأجلى من المعرف وكل تعريف هذا شأنه فاسد، وذلك إما بأن يكون المعرف والتعريف متساويين في المعرفة والجهالة ولكونهما متضايفين كتعريف الأب بمن له ولد، وإما بأن يكون التعريف أخفى من المعرف لتوقف معرفته على معرفة المعرف كتعريف الخبر بما احتمل الصدق والكذب على تقدير كون الصدق مطابقة الخبر للواقع والكذب عدم مطابقته، وإما بأن يكون أخفى من المعرف لكون معرفة معناه صعبا من معرفة مميز العرف كتعريف النار بأنه شيء يشبه النفس في اللطافة وعدم الرؤية. والنفس أخفى من النار لأن النار يمكن معرفتها بالاحساس دون النفس. وهو إشارة إلى دليل تطبيق المثال للمثل وهو في المآل دليل الصغرى المذكورة وتصويره بأن يقال: هذا التعريف ليس بأجلى من المعرف لأنه تعريف بالنفس والنفس أخفى منها. وكل ما ليس بأجلى من المعرف فهو فاسد لأن من شرائط صحة التعريف كونه أجلى من المعرف. وفيه تنبيه على أنه لا مجال لمنع الكبرى بل إنما يمنع الصغرى مستندا بتحرير التعريف أو المعرف بحيث يظهر به كون التعريف أجلى. وأشار بمن التبعيضية وطبيعة الجمع إلى كثرة الشرائط، وهي ثلاثة أمور: مساواة المعرف للمعرف الذي هو الجمع والمنع وخلوه عن المحالات وكونه أجلى من المعرف. وترك وظائف صاحب التعريف وهي منع الصغرى والمعارضة والنقض التحقيقيين وتغيير التعريف كلا أو بعضا إحالة على المقايسة وإشارة إلى قلة هذا النقض وجوابه.
And know that a real definition may be refuted by its not being clearer than the definiendum, and every definition with this state is invalid. This is either because the definiendum and the definition are equal in knowledge and ignorance due to being correlatives, like defining a father as one who has a son; or because the definition is more obscure than the definiendum due to its knowledge depending on knowledge of the definiendum, like defining report (khabar) as that which admits truth and falsehood on the assumption that truth is the conformity of the report to reality and falsehood is its non-conformity; or because it is more obscure than the definiendum due to the difficulty of understanding its meaning relative to the distinguishing criterion of custom, like defining fire as a thing resembling the soul in subtlety and invisibility. And the soul is more obscure than fire because fire can be known by sensation without the soul. This is an indication of the proof of applying the example to the similitude, and it is ultimately the proof of the minor premise mentioned, and its formulation: this definition is not clearer than the definiendum because it is a definition by the soul, and the soul is more obscure than it. And everything that is not clearer than the definiendum is invalid because from the conditions of the validity of a definition is its being clearer than the definiendum. And in it is a reminder that there is no room to deny the major premise; rather, one denies the minor premise based on refining the definition or the definiendum such that the definition appears clearer. And he indicated by the partitive 'min' and the form of the plural the abundance of conditions. They are three matters: equality of the definiendum to the definition in comprehensiveness and exclusivity, its being free from impossibilities, and its being clearer than the definiendum. And leaving the functions of the definer, which are denial of the minor premise, the two real objections and criticisms, and changing the definition in whole or in part—this refers to the analogy and is an indication of the rarity of this refutation and its answer.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage explains a specific type of refutation (naqd) of a definition: when the definition is not clearer (ajla) than the definiendum (mu'arraf). The author, while discussing conditions of a valid definition, states that a definition that is not clearer is invalid. He identifies three scenarios: 1) The definition and definiendum are equal in clarity, as in correlatives (mutadha'ifayn) like defining 'father' as 'one who has a son' — these are interdependent and equally known. 2) The definition is more obscure because understanding it depends on understanding the definiendum, e.g., defining 'report' (khabar) as 'that which admits truth and falsehood' when truth/falsehood are themselves defined by the report, creating a vicious circle. 3) The definition is more obscure due to the difficulty of its meaning relative to the definiendum, e.g., defining 'fire' as 'a thing resembling the soul in subtlety and invisibility' — fire, being sensible, is more known than the soul. The author then provides a logical proof: the definition is not clearer because it uses the soul, which is more obscure; and any definition that is not clearer is invalid because a condition of definition is that it be clearer. He notes that one cannot deny the major premise (the condition); rather, the opponent may deny the minor premise by refining the definition or the definiendum. Finally, he lists three general conditions of a valid definition: equality (the definition must be coextensive with the definiendum in generality and exclusivity), freedom from impossibilities (like circularity or contradiction), and being clearer. This naqd is rare, and the definer's only recourse is to deny the minor premise, object, or modify the definition.

Key Terms
النقض
أجلى
المتضايفان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is an example of a definition that is invalid because it is equal in clarity to the definiendum?
A) Defining fire as a thing resembling the soul in subtlety
B) Defining father as one who has a son
C) Defining report as that which admits truth and falsehood
D) Defining the soul as a substance that manages the body

Key Takeaway
A definition that is not clearer than the definiendum is invalid, whether due to equal clarity, dependence, or obscurity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the definition: 'The Qur'an is the speech of Allah, and speech is defined as the articulated sounds produced by the tongue.' Does this definition satisfy the clarity condition? Why or why not? Identify any potential violation based on the three types.
?

First Three Vices: Unfamiliar Words, Concomitant Meaning, and Ambiguous Words
The author lists and explains the first three prohibited practices in defining.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and avoid using unfamiliar words, concomitant meanings, and ambiguous words when constructing definitions in Islamic logic.

Core Idea
Definitions must be clear, direct, and unambiguous to avoid confusion.

In this lesson, we examine three of the four vices prohibited in definition: using unfamiliar or uncustomary words, intending the concomitant meaning instead of the literal meaning, and employing ambiguous words without clarification. These undermine the primary purpose of definition: to convey the essence clearly.

Guided Path
1
Recognize unfamiliar words
Identify terms that are not commonly used in the scholarly discourse. The author's example: 'fire is an element above the elements' uses an obscure term 'اسطقس'. Such words obscure the definition.
2
Identify concomitant meaning
Check if the definition relies on a property that necessarily accompanies the essence but is not the essence itself. Example: 'Zayd is the walking, speaking one' – walking implies animal, but animal is not directly stated. This is prohibited.
Literal signification (mutabaqa) is always valid; includent (tadamun) sometimes valid; concomitant (iltizam) never valid in definitions.
3
Detect ambiguous words
Look for words with multiple meanings (homonyms) used without specification. Example: 'science' used to define munazara, as 'ilm can mean knowledge or a discipline. This causes confusion.
The ambiguous word must be specified if used in definition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما استعمال الألفاظ الغريبة الغير المعتادة في التعريف مثل أن يقال النار اسطقس فوق الإستقسات. وإرادة المدلول الإلتزامي من التعريف أو من جزء من أجزائه، إذ الدلالة الإلتزامية مهجورة مطلقا والتضمنية مهجورة بعضا والمطابقية معتبرة مطلقا، كتعريف زيد بأنه الماشي الناطق، فإن للماشي يلزمه الحيوان فيدل على بعض ماهيته بالالتزام. واستعمال اللفظ المشترك الذي لا يصح إرادة كل واحد من معانيه، كالعلم في تعريف فن المناظرة بأنه علم يعرف به صحيح الدفع وفاسده. واستعمال اللفظ المجاز بدون القرينة. واعلم أن المجاز عند أهل الأصول لفظ استعمل في غير ما وضع له في اصطلاح به التخاطب العلاقة بينهما فيعم الكناية البيانية وهي لفظ أريد به لازم معناه مع جواز إرادته. وأما المجاز البياني فهو لفظ استعمل في غير ما وضع له في اصطلاح به التخاطب العلاقة بينهما بقرينة صارفة عما وضع له، فهذا لا يعم الكناية لكون القرينة جزءا منه.
As for the use of unfamiliar words not customary in definition, such as saying 'fire is an element above the elements.' And [the use] of intending the concomitant meaning from the definition or from a part of its parts, for the implicative signification is abandoned absolutely, the includent signification is partially abandoned, and the literal signification is considered absolutely, like defining Zayd as 'the walking, speaking one', for 'walking' entails animal, so it signifies part of his essence by implication. And the use of the ambiguous word which is not correct to intend each of its meanings, like 'science' in the definition of the art of disputation as 'a science by which the correct and incorrect of refutation and proof are known.' And the use of metaphorical expression without a context. And know that metaphor according to the scholars of usul is a word used in other than what it was placed for in the convention of discourse where there is a relation between them, and it includes the allusive trope (kinaya bayaniyya) which is a word by which its necessary meaning is intended while allowing the intention of its original meaning. As for the explicative metaphor (majaz bayani), it is a word used in other than what it was placed for in the convention of discourse where there is a relation between them, with a context diverting from its original meaning; this does not include the allusive trope because the context is part of it.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage enumerates four vices (afat) that invalidate a definition. The author discusses each: First, using unfamiliar (ghariba) words that are not customary, e.g., saying 'fire is an element above the elements' (استعمال الألفاظ الغريبة). The definition should use common, understood vocabulary. Second, intending the concomitant meaning (irada al-madlul al-iltizami) — that is, defining by a property that implies the essence but is not directly the essence. He distinguishes three types of signification: مطابقية (literal) is always valid; تضمنية (includent, i.e., part-whole) is sometimes abandoned; التزامية (implicative) is abandoned absolutely in definitions. Example: defining Zayd as 'the walking, speaking one' — walking implies animal (a necessary concomitant), but defining by a concomitant is not ideal. Third, using an ambiguous word (mushtarak) where it is not permissible to intend all meanings, e.g., using 'science' (al-ilm) in defining munazara; the term 'ilm has multiple senses. Fourth, using metaphorical expression (majaz) without a context (qarina) that clarifies the intended meaning. The author then explains the two types of majaz: (a) المجاز الأصولي (usuli metaphor) which includes الكناية البيانية (allusive trope, kinaya) — a word used for its necessary meaning while still allowing the original meaning; (b) المجاز البياني (rhetorical metaphor) which requires a context (qarina) to divert from the original meaning. The latter does not include kinaya because qarina is an integral part. All these vices undermine the clarity and precision required for a sound definition.

Key Terms
الألفاظ الغريبة
المدلول الإلتزامي
المشترك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is 'Zayd is the walking, speaking one' considered a flawed definition?
A) It uses an unfamiliar word.
B) It relies on a concomitant meaning (animal implied by walking) rather than direct essence.
C) It contains an ambiguous word.
D) It uses metaphor.

Key Takeaway
The first three vices – unfamiliar words, concomitant meaning, and ambiguous words – all obstruct clarity and must be avoided for a sound definition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Task 1: Consider the definition 'Salah is the religion's pillar' – identify if it contains any of the three vices discussed.

The Fourth Vice: Metaphor without Context and Types of Majaz
The author explains the prohibition of metaphor without context and elaborates on the two types of majaz.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why metaphor without context is a vice in definition and distinguish between usuli and bayani majaz.

Core Idea
Metaphor requires a contextual clue (qarina) to avoid ambiguity in definition.

The fourth vice is using a metaphorical expression without the necessary context (qarina) that indicates the intended meaning. The author then elaborates on two types of metaphor: usuli majaz, which includes kinaya (allusive trope), and bayani majaz, which requires a qarina to divert from the original meaning. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for proper definition.

Guided Path
1
Recognize metaphor without context
Identify if a term is used metaphorically, i.e., not in its original sense. If there is no accompanying clue to clarify the intended meaning, the definition is flawed.
2
Identify usuli majaz
According to scholars of usul, majaz includes kinaya (allusive trope), where a word is used for its necessary meaning while still allowing the original meaning. Example: 'He has many hands' meaning generosity.
Kinaya does not need a qarina because the original meaning is still possible.
3
Distinguish bayani majaz
Bayani majaz is a word used for a meaning other than its original due to a relation, but it must have a qarina that diverts from the original. This type does not include kinaya because qarina is essential.
Example: 'lion' used for a brave man.

Source Text

And [the use] of intending the concomitant meaning from the definition or from a part of its parts, for the implicative signification is abandoned absolutely, the includent signification is partially abandoned, and the literal signification is considered absolutely, like defining Zayd as 'the walking, speaking one', for 'walking' entails animal, so it signifies part of his essence by implication. As for the explicative metaphor (majaz bayani), it is a word used in other than what it was placed for in the convention of discourse where there is a relation between them, with a context diverting from its original meaning; this does not include the allusive trope because the context is part of it.

The Condition of Clarity: Definition Must Be Clearer
Author proves condition that definition must be clearer than definiendum.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify whether a definition satisfies the condition of being clearer (ajlā) than the definiendum and reconstruct the logical proof that a definition not clearer is invalid.

Core Idea
A definition that is not clearer than its definiendum fails its clarifying purpose.

In this passage, the author establishes a fundamental condition for any sound definition: it must be clearer than the thing being defined. He provides a simple logical proof and discusses why a definition that defines by the soul (or itself) is invalid. Understanding this condition helps you evaluate definitions in Islamic sciences, such as definitions of key fiqh terms or 'illa in qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim and the proof
Find the statement that a definition must be clearer than the definiendum. Then trace the logical argument: the minor premise (this definition is not clearer because it defines by the soul) and the major premise (every definition not clearer is invalid).
2
Understand the proof structure
The author uses a conditional syllogism: if a definition is not clearer, it is not valid. The definer can only deny the minor premise by showing the definition is actually clearer.
3
Test an example
Consider a definition like 'the soul is the essence of life' – is it clearer? The author says no, because the soul is more hidden. Apply this to definitions in usul al-fiqh, e.g., 'the 'illa is the effective cause' – is that clearer?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهو إشارة إلى دليل تطبيق المثال للمثل وهو في المآل دليل الصغرى المذكورة وتصويره . بأن يقال هذا التعريف ليس بأجلى من المعرف لأنه تعريف بالنفس والنفس أخفى منها . وكل ماهو كذلك ليس بأجلى من المعرف فهو ليس بأجلى ( ومن شرائط ملحة التعريف كونه ) أى كون التعريف (أجلى من المعرف) يجوز أن يكون متعلقا بقوله قد ينقض التعريف وأن يكون متعلقا بقوله والنفس أخفى وعلى التقديرين فهو إشارة إلى دليل الكبرى المنطوية بأن يقال وكل ما ليس بأجلى من المعرف فهو فاسد لأن من شرائط صحة التعريف الخ وفيه تنبيه على أنه لا مجال لمنع الكبرى بل إنما يمنع الصغرى مستندا بتحرير التعريف أو المعرف بحيث يظهر به كون التعريف أجلى ، وأشار بمن التبعيضية وطبيعة الجمع إلى كثرة الشرائط، وهى ثلاثة أمور : مساواة المعرف للمعرف الذى هو الجمع والمنع وخلوه عن المحالات وكونه أجلى من المعرف وترك وظائف صاحب التعريف وهى منع الصغرى والمعارضة والنقض التحقيقيين وتغيير التعريف كلا أو بعضا إحالة على المقايسة وإشارة إلى قلة هذا النقض وجوابه وأما استعمال الألفاظ الغريبة في التعريف مثل أن يقال النار اسطقس فوق الإستقسات، والإستعمال ذكر اللفظ وإرادة المعنى منه مطلقا و الغرابة كون الكلمة وحشية غير ظاهرة المعي ولا مأنوسة الاستعمال كتكأ كأنم وافر نقعوا وإرادة المدلول الإلتزامى من التعريف أو من جزء من أجزائه إذ الدلالة الإلزامية مهجورة مطلقا والتضمنية مهجورة بعضا والمطابقية معتبرة مطلقا كتعريف زيد بأنه الماشي الناطق ، فان للماشي يلزمه الحيوان كما لا يخفى فيدل على بعض ماهيته بالالتزام واستعمال اللفظ المشترك فيه الذى لا يصح إرادة كل واحد من معانيه كالعلم في تعريف فن المناظرة بأنه علم يعرف به صحيح الدفع وفاسده أو استعمال اللفظ المجاز بدون الفرينة قيد للأخيرين ، ومن جمله قيدا للأربعة فقد أخطأ كمالا يخفى على من له تأمل صادق . اعلم أن المجاز عند أهل الأصول لفظ استعمل في غير ما وضع له في اصطلاح به التخاطب العلاقة بينهما فيعم الكنانة البيانية ، وهي لفظ أريد به لازم معناه مع جواز إرادته . والمجاز البياني لكون معرفة معنى النار سهلا من معرفة معنى النفس لأن معنى النار من المحسوسات دون معنى النفس ومن شرائط صحة التعريف كونه أجلى من المعرف على أنه لا مجال هنالمنع الكبرى بل يمنع الصغرى مستندا بتحرير التعريف أو المعرف بحيث يظهر به كون التعريف أجلى من المعرف وأما استعمال الألفظ الغريبة الغير المعتادة وإرادة المدلول الإلتزامي إن قلت إرادة للدلول الإلتزامي إن كانت قصدية فهي الحقيقة فى استعمال المجازوإن كانت تبعية فما الفائدة في إرادته إذ هو ليس بمدخل ولا مخرج، ولا إيضاح فى الإرادة التبعية كما لا يخفى . قلت يختار أنه مراد تبعا للاطلاق على الذاتى لكن لما كانت مهجورة فى التعريف مطلقا أو في الحد مطلقا أو في النام مطلقا أو في الحد التام أزالت حسنه فاعرف واستعمال اللفظ للمشترك الذى لا يصح إرادة كل من معانيه أو المجاز الأصولي ، وهو لفظ استعمل في غير ما وضع له في اصطلاح به التخاطب العلاقة بينهما فيهم الكناية البيانية ، وهو لفظ أريد به لازم معناه مع جواز إرادته . وأما المجاز البياني: فهو لفظ استعمل في غير ما وضع له في اصطلاح به التخاطب العلاقة بينهما بقرينة صارفة عما وضع له فهذا لايعم البكتابة لكون القرينة جزءا منه ومباينة الجنسها فاعرف بدون القرينة وهو لفظ استعمل في غير ما وضع له في اصطلاح به التخاطب العلاقة مع قرينة ما نعة عن إرادته والقرينة المطلقة ما يفسح عن المراد لا بالوضع، وهى إما مانعة أو معينة : أما المانعة فهي ما يمتنع عنده إرادة للعنى الحقيقى حما أو عقلا أو شرعا أو عادة ، وأما المعينة فهى ما يعين المراد ويوضحه ، فالمجاز لا بد له من قرينتين مانعة ومعينة ، والكناية لا بد لها أيضا من قرينتين قرينة للانتقال ، وقرينة معينة للمراد والمشترك لا بد له من قرينة معينة له ، وأما الحقيقة فلا يلزم أن يكون لها قرينة الواضحة المعينة للمراد صفة للقرينة ، واحترز به عن القرينة المانعة للمجاز لأنها داخلة فى مفهوم المجاز فلا يصبح المجاز بدونها ولا يصح التعريف المشتمل للمجاز بدونها فهو أى كل واحد من هذه الأمور يذهب من الإذهاب حسن التعريف لا صحته إذ السامع يحتاج إلى الاستفسار في هذه الأمور وهو غير مناسب لمقام التعريف ، ولأن لكل معنى لوازم متعددة فلا يتعين اللازم الذي أريد في المدلول الالتزامى، وعدم تعين المراد في المشترك تتزاحم معانيه وعدم تعينه في المجاز ولعدم علمه بالمدلول في الغريب ، وكذا يجب الاحتراز عن استعمال اللفظ الغير العربي واللفظ المستدرك واللفظ الضعيف بناء وإعرابا وعن التخصيص بلا مخصص ، وينبغي أن يعلم أن هذه الأمور إنما تذهب حسن التعريف لا صحته في التعريف الحقيقى ، وأما فى التعريف اللفظى ، فهو يذهب صحته قطعا وتصوير النقض بهذه الأمور أن يقال إن هذا التعريف مثلا مشتمل على اللفظ الغريب أو على المدلول الالتزامى أو على اللفظ المشترك بدون قرينة معينة أو على المجاز بدونها ، وكل ما كان كذلك ، فهو ليس بجيد . وأما الجواب من صاحب التعريف فيعرف بالمقايسة فتأمل واستخرج والظاهر أن النقض بأحد هذه الأمور نقض إجمالى مجازى لأن النقض إبطال الدليل أو التعريف أو التقسم ولا إبطال هنا فلا يكون حقيقيا إذا كان للعنى للقصود من هذه الألفاظ أحلى من للعرف وأما إذا لم يكن أجلى فيعترض على التعريف ببطلانه لا بانتفاء حسنه فقط . اعلم أن استعمال أحد هذه الأمور في التعريف إنما يذهب حسن التعريف لاصحته إذا كان التعريف جامعا ومانها وخاليا عن المحالات ، وكان أحلى من المعرف تقوله إذا كان للعنى المقصود أحلى من المعرف الواضحة المعينة للمراد قيد للآخرين إذ لا معنى للقرينة في الألفاظ الغربة . وأما إرادة المدلول الالتزامي فالمسمى قرينة معينة لها فلا يتصور أنفكاكه فتأمل فهو أي استعمال كل من المذكورات وكذا استعمال اللفظ الوحشى القير العذب واللفظ المستدرك واللفظ الضعيف بناؤه أو إعرابه غلط لفظى يذهب حسن التعريف لا صحته إذ السامع يحتاج إلى الاستفادة من المراد وهو غير مناسب المقام التعريف وذا لتعدد المدلول وعدم تعين المراد في المشترك ولعدم تعينه في المجازو لعدم علمه بالمدلول أصلا في الغريب وأما إزالة الإرادة فلكونها مهجورة في التعريفات عند المحققين وأما القرينة الصارفة فهى أعم من المعينة وشرطية الأخص تستلزم شرطية الأعم مع أنها داخلة في مفهوم المجاز البياني وأما إذا كان التعريف لفظيا فيذهب بذلك الأربعة المذكورة صحته وبالأربعة التي ذكرناها حسنه قتبصر، وقوله إذا كان المعنى المقصود أجلى من المعرف لاحاجة إليه إذ قيد الحيثية معتبر في الجميع وإلا لاحتيج إلى أن يقال ولم يستلزم لفسادها ، وتقريره أن هذا التعريف مشتمل على لفظ كنا حسن والمنوع الجارية فى هذا الدليل وأسانيدها غير خفية على من له حظ فى العربية
And it is an indication of the proof applying the example to the like, and it is in the final analysis a proof of the mentioned minor premise. Its representation is that it is said: This definition is not clearer than the definiendum because it is a definition by the soul, and the soul is more hidden than it. And everything that is like that—not clearer than the definiendum—is not clearer. (And among the conditions of a sound definition is that it be) meaning the definition (clearer than the definiendum). It may be related to his saying 'it may refute the definition' and may be related to his saying 'and the soul is more hidden'. In both cases it is an indication of the implied major premise, that it is said: Everything that is not clearer than the definiendum is invalid because among the conditions of the correctness of the definition is etc. And in it there is a reminder that there is no room to deny the major premise, rather the minor premise is denied based on reformulating the definition or the definiendum such that the definition appears clearer. And he indicated by the partitive 'min' and the nature of plurality the abundance of conditions, and they are three matters: equality of the definiens to the definiendum which is inclusion and exclusion, its being free of impossibilities, and its being clearer than the definiendum. And leaving the duties of the definer, which are denial of the minor premise, objection, and investigative refutation, and changing the definition wholly or partially, is referral to comparison and an indication of the rarity of this refutation and its answer. And as for using strange words in the definition, such as saying 'fire is an element above elements'; and usage is mentioning the word and intending its meaning absolutely, and strangeness is the word being unfamiliar, not apparent in meaning, and not customary in usage, like 'taka ka'anam wa fir naqa'u'. And intending the implicative meaning from the definition or from part of its parts, for implicative indication is abandoned absolutely, and inclusive indication is partially abandoned, and conformative indication is considered absolutely, like defining Zayd as 'the walking speaker', for 'walking' necessitates 'animal' as is clear, so it indicates part of his essence by implication. And using the ambiguous word where it is not valid to intend each of its meanings, like 'knowledge' in defining the art of disputation as 'knowledge by which sound and unsound argument is known'. Or using metaphorical word without a qarina, which is a condition for the last two, and whoever includes it as a condition for all four has erred, as is not hidden to one who has sincere reflection. Know that majaz according to the uṣūliyyūn is a word used in other than what it was coined for in the convention of discourse with a relationship between them, and it includes rhetorical kināyah, which is a word by which its necessary meaning is intended while it is permissible to intend its original meaning. And the figurative majaz because knowing the meaning of fire is easier than knowing the meaning of the soul, because the meaning of fire is among sensibles while the meaning of the soul is not. And from the conditions of the correctness of the definition is that it be clearer than the definiendum, on the basis that there is no room to deny the major premise, rather the minor premise is denied based on reformulating the definition or the definiendum such that the definition appears clearer than the definiendum. And as for using strange words that are unusual and intending the implicative meaning: If you say, the intending of the implicative meaning, if it is intentional, then it is actually using majaz; if it is subsidiary, what benefit is there in intending it since it is neither an entry nor an exit, and there is no clarification in subsidiary intending as is clear. I say: It is chosen that it is intended subsidiary to the absolute statement about the essential, but since it is abandoned in definition absolutely, or in the definition (ḥadd) absolutely, or in the nam (?) absolutely, or in the complete definition, it removes its beauty, so recognize. And using the ambiguous word that is not valid to intend each of its meanings, or the uṣūlī majaz, which is a word used in other than what it was coined for in the convention of discourse with a relationship between them, and it includes rhetorical kināyah, which is a word by which its necessary meaning is intended while it is permissible to intend its original meaning. As for figurative majaz: it is a word used in other than what it was coined for in the convention of discourse with a relationship between them with a qarina that turns away from what it was coined for; so this does not include kināyah because the qarina is part of it and its genus is different, so recognize. Without the qarina, it is a word used in other than what it was coined for in the convention of discourse with a relationship with a qarina that prevents its intended meaning. And the absolute qarina is what reveals the intended meaning not by coinage, and it is either preventing or specifying. As for the preventing, it is that by which intending the literal meaning is prevented, whether by sense, reason, law, or custom. As for the specifying, it is that which specifies the intended meaning and clarifies it. Thus majaz necessarily has two qarinas: a preventing and a specifying. Kināyah also necessarily has two qarinas: a qarina for transfer and a specifying qarina for the intended meaning. The ambiguous word necessarily has a specifying qarina for it. As for the literal, it is not necessary that it have a clarifying specifying qarina for the intended meaning, which is a qualification of the qarina, and he guards thereby against the preventing qarina for majaz because it is included in the concept of majaz, so majaz is not valid without it. And the definition that includes majaz is not correct without it. So each one of these matters removes the beauty of the definition, not its correctness, because the hearer needs to ask for clarification in these matters, and that is not appropriate for the context of definition; and because every meaning has multiple necessary concomitants, so the necessary that is intended in the implicative meaning is not determined; and lack of determination of the intended in the ambiguous word results in its meanings conflicting; and lack of determination of the intended in majaz; and due to lack of knowledge of the meaning at all in the strange word. Likewise, one must avoid using non-Arabic words, and the obsolete word, and the weak word in construction and parsing, and specification without a specifier. And it should be known that these matters remove the beauty of the definition, not its correctness, in the real definition. As for the verbal definition, it removes its correctness absolutely. And the depiction of the criticism (naqd) by these matters is that it is said: This definition, for example, includes a strange word, or an implicative meaning, or an ambiguous word without a specifying qarina, or a majaz without it. And everything that is like that is not good. As for the answer from the definer, it is known by comparison, so reflect and extract. And it appears that the criticism by these matters is a summary figurative criticism because criticism is invalidation of the proof, definition, or division, and there is no invalidation here, so it is not real. If the intended meaning of these words is clearer than the definiendum, then it is a criticism of the definition as invalid, not just lack of beauty. Know that using one of these matters in the definition removes the beauty of the definition, not its correctness, if the definition is inclusive and exclusive and free of impossibilities and clearer than the definiendum. You say: if the intended meaning is clearer than the definiendum, the clarifying specifying qarina is a condition for the others, for there is no meaning to the qarina in the strange words. As for intending the implicative meaning, the one who specifies the qarina for it cannot be separated, so reflect. So each one of the mentioned usages, and likewise using an unfamiliar word, and the obsolete word, and the weak word in construction or parsing, a verbal error, removes the beauty of the definition, not its correctness, because the hearer needs to ascertain the intended meaning, and that is not appropriate for the context of definition, and due to multiplicity of meanings and lack of determination of the intended in the ambiguous word, and lack of determination in the majaz, and lack of knowledge of the meaning at all in the strange word. As for removing the intended meaning, it is because it is abandoned in definitions among the verifiers. As for the turning qarina, it is more general than the specifying one, and the conditionality of the specific entails the conditionality of the general, with it being included in the concept of figurative majaz. And if the definition is verbal, then the four mentioned remove its correctness, and the four we mentioned remove its beauty, so be discerning. And his statement: 'if the intended meaning is clearer than the definiendum' is unnecessary, for the condition of respect is considered in all, otherwise it would need to be said that it does not entail its invalidity. And its explanation: this definition includes a word that is like beautiful, and the prevalent prohibitions in this proof and their supports are not hidden to one who has a portion in Arabic.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the conditions of a sound definition (ta'rīf). It begins by discussing a proof that a definition must be clearer (ajlā) than the definiendum. The author explains that if a definition defines something by itself (al-nafs), it is not clearer, and thus invalid. The proof uses a conditional syllogism: if a definition is not clearer than the definiendum, it is not valid. The major premise is that a valid definition must be clearer. The minor premise is that this definition is not clearer. The author notes that the opponent cannot deny the major premise but may deny the minor by showing the definition is actually clearer. He then lists three general conditions for a definition: equality (musāwāt) in inclusion and exclusion, freedom from impossibilities, and being clearer than the definiendum. He also mentions the duties of the definer in responding to objections. Then the passage turns to four specific usages that spoil the beauty (ḥusn) of a definition, though not necessarily its correctness: 1) strange words (alfāẓ gharība), 2) implicative meaning (dalāla iltizāmiyya), 3) ambiguous words (al-lafẓ al-mushtarak), and 4) metaphorical usage (majāz) without a clarifying qarīna. For each, examples are given. Strange words are those unfamiliar and not commonly understood, like the nonsense example 'tak ka' anam wa fir naqa'u'. Implicative meaning refers to a definition that indirectly indicates a part of the essence, like defining Zayd as 'the walking speaker' which implies 'animal' by necessity; such indication is abandoned in definitions. Ambiguous words are those with multiple meanings that cannot all be intended simultaneously, like 'knowledge' in a definition of dialectic. Metaphorical usage without a qarīna is also problematic. The author then delves into a detailed discussion of types of majāz (uṣūlī vs. bayānī) and qarīna (preventing vs. specifying). He explains that kināyah (indirect suggestion) is included in uṣūlī majāz but not in bayānī majāz. A proper definition must avoid these pitfalls because they confuse the hearer and defeat the purpose of clarification. The passage also distinguishes between real definitions (ḥaqīqī) and verbal definitions (lafẓī). In real definitions, these issues only affect beauty; in verbal definitions, they affect correctness. Finally, it discusses how to formulate an objection (naqḍ) based on these issues and how the definer might respond, emphasizing that such a criticism is not a true invalidation but a judgment of lack of beauty, unless the definition is not clearer.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why is defining 'the soul' by 'the soul' invalid?
A) It uses a foreign word.
B) It is not clearer because the soul is more hidden.
C) It lacks a differentia.
D) It is too long.

Key Takeaway
A valid definition must be clearer than the definiendum; otherwise it fails its clarifying purpose.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Examine the definition of 'qiyas' from al-Ghazali: 'Qiyas is the application of a ruling from an original case to a new case due to a shared cause.' Is this definition clearer than the definiendum? Why or why not?
?
Construct a definition of 'hukm shar'i' that satisfies the condition of being clearer than the definiendum. Then check if it is indeed clearer.

Hadd and Rasm
intermediate
7 min
Four Usages That Spoil the Beauty of a Definition
Author enumerates four usages that spoil definition's beauty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify each of the four problematic usages (strange words, implicative meaning, ambiguous words, metaphor without qarina) in a definition and explain why they spoil its beauty.

Core Idea
A definition must be immediately clear; strange words, ambiguity, or indirectness defeat its purpose.

The author lists four specific usages that, while they may not always invalidate a definition, ruin its beauty and make it unsuitable for clarifying. These are using strange (unfamiliar) words, intending the implicative meaning, using ambiguous words without a clarifying qarina, and using metaphor without a qarina. Understanding these helps you produce clear definitions in Islamic scholarship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four problematic usages
List them: 1) strange words (alfaz ghariba), 2) implicative meaning (dalala iltizamiyya), 3) ambiguous words (lafz mushtarak), 4) metaphor without qarina (majaz bila qarina).
2
Understand why each is problematic
For each, the author explains that the hearer needs extra effort to understand, which is contrary to the purpose of definition. Strange words are unfamiliar; implicative meaning does not directly indicate the essence; ambiguous words cause confusion; metaphor without qarina leaves multiple possibilities.
3
Test with Islamic examples
Consider a definition of 'salat' as 'a ritual practice' (strange? not really). Or defining 'iman' as 'that which necessitates action' (implicative). Determine which category it falls into.

وهو إشارة إلى دليل تطبيق المثال للمثل وهو في المآل دليل الصغرى المذكورة وتصويره . بأن يقال هذا التعريف ليس بأجلى من المعرف لأنه تعريف بالنفس والنفس أخفى منها . وكل ماهو كذلك ليس بأجلى من المعرف فهو ليس بأجلى ( ومن شرائط ملحة التعريف كونه ) أى كون التعريف (أجلى من المعرف) يجوز أن يكون متعلقا بقوله قد ينقض التعريف وأن يكون متعلقا بقوله والنفس أخفى وعلى التقديرين فهو إشارة إلى دليل الكبرى المنطوية بأن يقال وكل ما ليس بأجلى من المعرف فهو فاسد لأن من شرائط صحة التعريف الخ وفيه تنبيه على أنه لا مجال لمنع الكبرى بل إنما يمنع الصغرى مستندا بتحرير التعريف أو المعرف بحيث يظهر به كون التعريف أجلى ، وأشار بمن التبعيضية وطبيعة الجمع إلى كثرة الشرائط، وهى ثلاثة أمور : مساواة المعرف للمعرف الذى هو الجمع والمنع وخلوه عن المحالات وكونه أجلى من المعرف وترك وظائف صاحب التعريف وهى منع الصغرى والمعارضة والنقض التحقيقيين وتغيير التعريف كلا أو بعضا إحالة على المقايسة وإشارة إلى قلة هذا النقض وجوابه وأما استعمال الألفاظ الغريبة في التعريف مثل أن يقال النار اسطقس فوق الإستقسات، والإستعمال ذكر اللفظ
